Al-Kaabi's Objections on Divine Creation
Al-Kaabi presents five objections against God creating evil acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key objections raised by al-Kaabi against the Maturidi view that God creates all things, including evil acts.

Core Idea
Al-Kaabi argues that God's creation cannot include evil because that would contradict His praise and justice.

Before we can appreciate Maturidi's refutation, we need to hear the objections clearly. Al-Kaabi, a Mu'tazili theologian, raises several scriptural and rational arguments to exclude evil acts from God's creation. This lesson presents those objections as the starting point for the discussion.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Kaabi's first objection
Al-Kaabi argues that the verse 'Creator of everything' (Qur'an 6:102) is a praise (imtidaah), so it cannot include blameworthy acts like reviling God or killing prophets.
2
Second objection: God punishes disbelief
Al-Kaabi says God blames disbelief and punishes it; if He were its creator, that would be inconsistent with His justice.
3
Third and fourth objections
He claims the verse is specific to good things, and that the pronoun 'He' excludes human actions. He also notes that ugly deeds were not mentioned by the Prophet.
These objections rely on a restricted interpretation of 'everything'.
4
Fifth objection and the hadith
Al-Kaabi argues that the Qadariyya (those who deny divine creation of actions) are called the Magians of this ummah, implying his view is orthodox.
He cites the hadith to support his position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم ذكر الكعبي أسئلتنا من ذلك قوله تعالى: خالق كل شيء، وأعمال العباد أشياء. فزعم أن ذا امتداح، وليس ذلك في شتم نفسه ولا في الكفر به ولا في قتل الأنبياء. والثاني أنه عاب الكفر وعذب عليه، ولا يجوز ذلك على ما يفعله. وقال: خصصنا أيضاً بما تلونا من الآيات. ودليل ذلك أنه لم يدخل هو في ذلك، وهو شيء؛ مع وجود آيات ذلك مخرجها، وهي خاصة. وبعد، فإن القبائح لم تذكر في هذا على عهد رسول الله، وإنما ذكر في الجواهر المورثة؛ وقال: بل قول المجوس أن الله أراد شيئًا مما هي محرمة في الإسلام، ولذلك قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة». قال الشيخ رحمه الله: نقول وبالله التوفيق إذ ثبت أن الآية بحق الامتداح، كان في خروج شيء من الكائنات امتداحاً بغير الذي له، أو بما يشاركه فيه كل ضعيف؛ لأنه لو أراد كلية الأشياء ولم يكن خلقها، فامتدح بغير الذي له، وذلك كذب. وفي إخراج البعض مساواة غيره في أنه صانع كل شيء، يريد ما لا صنع له فيه، وذلك فاسد. مع ما لو جاز ذلك على الصرف إلى الغير الذي هو فعل للغير ليجوز أن يقال: ليس بخالق شيء، على أنه ليس بخالق ما هو فعل لغيره. فإذ كان وصفا له بالذم والعبودة ثبت أن الأول وصف له بالمدح والربوبية، وفي التخصيص إيجاب الأول. وأيضا إنه قال: هو رب كل شيء وإله كل شيء، وهو على كل شيء وكيل، ولم يجز إخراج شيء عن ذلك؛ وإن كان لا يليق القول به على التخصيص لقبح، نحو أن يقال: رب الخبائث وإله القبائح ووكيل الشياطين وإبليس، وقائم على كل نتن وقذر، فمثله الأول، وإن كان يقبح على التخصيص في أشياء من حيث التسمية. وبهذا الوجه الذي قال شهدت المجوس والزنادقة أن الله تعالى لم يخلق مؤذياً ولا فسادًا، ولا أمات وليا ولا أ?سى عدوا ولا أبقى الشياطين، ولا أعطى من يعلم أنه يشتمه ويصد عن طاعته أحدا قوة. ذكرنا ذلك ليعلموا أن أصل الاعتزال مقدر عن ذلك؛ إذ إليه فزعهم عند مخالفتهم المفهوم من القرآن ومما جرى عليه قول الإسلام، ولذلك قال رسول الله عليه السلام: «القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة».
Then al-Kaabi mentioned our questions: Among that is His saying: 'Creator of everything', and the deeds of servants are things. So he claimed that this is a praise, and that is not in reviling Himself nor in disbelief in Him nor in killing the prophets. And the second is that He blamed disbelief and punished it, and that is not permissible for what He does. And he said: We also specified by the verses we recited. And the proof of that is that 'He' is not included in that, and 'He' is a thing; while there are verses whose meaning is that they are specific. And after that, ugly deeds were not mentioned in this from the covenant of the Messenger of God, but mentioned in inherited precious jewels. And he said: Rather the saying of the Magians is that God willed something of what is forbidden in Islam, and therefore the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: 'The Qadariyya are the Magians of this community.' The Shaykh, may God have mercy on him, said: We say, and with God is success: When it is established that the verse is truly for praise, it would be in excluding something from existences a praise for other than what belongs to Him, or by what every weakling shares with Him. Because if He intended all things and did not create them, then He would praise for other than what belongs to Him, and that is a lie. And in excluding some, it equals others in that He is the maker of everything, but He intends what He has no making in, and that is corrupt. Moreover, if that were allowed for referring to another who is action for another, it would be permissible to say: He is not a creator of anything, on the basis that He is not the creator of what is the action of another. So since that would be a description of Him with blame and servitude, it is established that the first is a description of Him with praise and lordship, and in the specification it necessitates the first. And also He said: 'He is the Lord of everything and the God of everything, and He is over everything a guardian', and it is not permissible to exclude anything from that; even if it is not fitting to say it with specification due to ugliness, such as saying: Lord of filths and God of obscenities and Guardian of devils and Iblis, and Standing over every rot and filth, so the like of the first, even if it is ugly when specified for some things in terms of naming. And by this aspect that he said, the Magians and heretics testified that God did not create anything harmful nor corruption, nor caused a saint to die nor made an enemy [weak?], nor left the devils, nor gave power to anyone whom He knows will revile Him and turn away from obedience. We mentioned that so that they know that the origin of Mu'tazilism is derived from that; for they have recourse to it when they contradict what is understood from the Qur'an and what the saying of Islam has proceeded upon, and therefore the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: 'The Qadriyya are the Magians of this community.'
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer structure. The author first reports objections from al-Kaabi against the Maturidi view that God is the creator of all things, including evil acts. Al-Kaabi argues that the verse 'Creator of everything' (Qur'an 6:102) is only praise and does not include things like reviling God or killing prophets, because those would not be praiseworthy. He also argues that God blames and punishes disbelief, so He cannot be its creator. He claims that the verse is specifically for good things, not evil acts. He further argues that the pronoun 'He' in the verse refers only to God, not to human actions, and that ugly deeds were not discussed by the Prophet. He cites a hadith that Qadariyya are the Magians of this ummah. The author then responds: If the verse is for praise, then excluding some existences from creation would mean God is praised for what He did not create, which is false. If some things are excluded, that makes others equal to God in creating those things, which is corrupt. If we say acts of servants are not created by God, one could deny God's creation entirely. Such specification would make God blameworthy. Since the verse 'He is Lord of everything' (Qur'an 6:164) and similar verses include everything, we cannot exclude anything, even if it sounds ugly to specify particular objects. The Magians and heretics took this view to its conclusion, denying that God creates harmful things. The author concludes that Mu'tazilism originates from such divergences from the plain meaning of the Qur'an and the consensus of Islam, confirming the hadith about Qadariyya being Magians.

Key Terms
خالق كل شيء
امتداح
قدرية
مجوس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God cannot create evil because He is praised and punishes evil.
Correction: Al-Kaabi's objection wrongly assumes that divine creation of evil entails divine approval or injustice. Maturidi responds by affirming God's absolute sovereignty while distinguishing creation from moral approval.

Checkpoint
According to al-Kaabi, why does the verse 'Creator of everything' not include evil acts?
A) Evil acts are not things
B) The verse is a praise, and evil acts are blameworthy
C) The Prophet forbade discussing evil acts
D) The Magians already used the same argument

Key Takeaway
Al-Kaabi's objections rest on the assumption that divine creation of evil contradicts God's praise and justice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter suffering or evil in your life, do you ever find yourself subtly denying God's complete control over that event to protect your image of a 'good' God? How does Al-Kaabi's instinct to exclude evil from God's creation mirror a tendency in your own heart? Commit to reciting 'Creator of everything' while consciously including the difficult moments.
?
Al-Kaabi argued that God cannot create what He punishes. Have you ever assumed that your sins are somehow outside God's plan because you cannot bear the thought that He willed them? How does this lesson challenge your desire to limit God's sovereignty to preserve your own comfort? Write down one area you have been slow to submit to His complete will.
?
The hadith equates denying God's creation of actions with Magian dualism. Are there areas of your life where you functionally believe in two sources—God for good, and something else for evil? How can you repent from this subtle shirk and acknowledge that everything, including your trials, comes from Him? Resolve to thank Him for a specific difficulty today.

Divine Decree
intermediate

Maturidi's Refutation of Al-Kaabi
Maturidi refutes al-Kaabi's objections with logical arguments for absolute divine creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's logical refutation of al-Kaabi's objections, establishing that God is the creator of all things including evil acts.

Core Idea
If God is not the creator of all things, then praise for creation would be false and others would share in divinity.

Maturidi now responds to al-Kaabi's objections with a series of logical arguments. He shows that restricting God's creation leads to absurd consequences: either God is praised for what He did not do, or others become creators alongside Him. This lesson unpacks Maturidi's rigorous reasoning and its implications for divine unity.

Guided Path
1
First argument: praise requires creation
If the verse is praise, then excluding some things means God is praised for what He did not create, which is false.
2
Second argument: avoiding associationism
If some things are not created by God, then others are equal to Him in creating those things, which is corrupt (fasid).
3
Third argument: slippery slope
If we exclude human acts, one could deny God creates anything, leading to atheism.
4
Fourth argument: specification leads to blame
Specifying God as Lord of all but excluding ugly things would make Him blameworthy, which is impossible.
5
Conclusion: Magians and Mu'tazilism
Maturidi shows that al-Kaabi's view leads to the same conclusion as Magians, confirming the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم ذكر الكعبي أسئلتنا من ذلك قوله تعالى: خالق كل شيء، وأعمال العباد أشياء. فزعم أن ذا امتداح، وليس ذلك في شتم نفسه ولا في الكفر به ولا في قتل الأنبياء. والثاني أنه عاب الكفر وعذب عليه، ولا يجوز ذلك على ما يفعله. وقال: خصصنا أيضاً بما تلونا من الآيات. ودليل ذلك أنه لم يدخل هو في ذلك، وهو شيء؛ مع وجود آيات ذلك مخرجها، وهي خاصة. وبعد، فإن القبائح لم تذكر في هذا على عهد رسول الله، وإنما ذكر في الجواهر المورثة؛ وقال: بل قول المجوس أن الله أراد شيئًا مما هي محرمة في الإسلام، ولذلك قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة». قال الشيخ رحمه الله: نقول وبالله التوفيق إذ ثبت أن الآية بحق الامتداح، كان في خروج شيء من الكائنات امتداحاً بغير الذي له، أو بما يشاركه فيه كل ضعيف؛ لأنه لو أراد كلية الأشياء ولم يكن خلقها، فامتدح بغير الذي له، وذلك كذب. وفي إخراج البعض مساواة غيره في أنه صانع كل شيء، يريد ما لا صنع له فيه، وذلك فاسد. مع ما لو جاز ذلك على الصرف إلى الغير الذي هو فعل للغير ليجوز أن يقال: ليس بخالق شيء، على أنه ليس بخالق ما هو فعل لغيره. فإذ كان وصفا له بالذم والعبودة ثبت أن الأول وصف له بالمدح والربوبية، وفي التخصيص إيجاب الأول. وأيضا إنه قال: هو رب كل شيء وإله كل شيء، وهو على كل شيء وكيل، ولم يجز إخراج شيء عن ذلك؛ وإن كان لا يليق القول به على التخصيص لقبح، نحو أن يقال: رب الخبائث وإله القبائح ووكيل الشياطين وإبليس، وقائم على كل نتن وقذر، فمثله الأول، وإن كان يقبح على التخصيص في أشياء من حيث التسمية. وبهذا الوجه الذي قال شهدت المجوس والزنادقة أن الله تعالى لم يخلق مؤذياً ولا فسادًا، ولا أمات وليا ولا أ?سى عدوا ولا أبقى الشياطين، ولا أعطى من يعلم أنه يشتمه ويصد عن طاعته أحدا قوة. ذكرنا ذلك ليعلموا أن أصل الاعتزال مقدر عن ذلك؛ إذ إليه فزعهم عند مخالفتهم المفهوم من القرآن ومما جرى عليه قول الإسلام، ولذلك قال رسول الله عليه السلام: «القدرية مجوس هذه الأمة».

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God's creation of evil means He approves of evil or is unjust.

Checkpoint
What is the main logical flaw Maturidi identifies in al-Kaabi's objection?
A) Al-Kaabi misunderstands the Arabic grammar
B) Excluding some things from creation leads to shirk or false praise
C) The hadith is weak in authenticity
D) Al-Kaabi did not consider the attributes of God

Key Takeaway
Maturidi shows that absolute divine creation is necessary to preserve God's praise, lordship, and unity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face hardship or commit a sin, do you truly believe that God created that moment for a wise purpose, or do you subtly shift blame to others or yourself, denying His absolute creation? How will you repent and affirm His lordship over every detail of your life?
?
The Magians argued that God does not create harmful things. In what ways do you complain about your trials as if they were not from Him? Will you accept His decree over things you find ugly, trusting His wisdom that He is Lord of all? What practical step will you take to cultivate contentment with His creation of both good and difficult circumstances?
?
Maturidi warns that specifying God's creation only to good things leads to shirk. Examine your own heart: do you praise God only when things go well, and attribute failures to yourself or others? How does this passage challenge you to see His hand in every event, good and bad? What concrete change will you make in your attitude towards difficult situations starting today?

Exposing Inconsistency: The Analogy of Divine Presence
Maturidi refutes an objection using an analogy of spatial presence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's method of refuting an opponent's deflection by exposing inconsistency in their own principles.

Core Idea
Inconsistency in general statements reveals flawed theology.

Maturidi encounters an opponent who avoids the direct ruling of a verse by shifting to a discussion about types of actions. To expose the flaw, Maturidi draws an analogy: just as someone who says 'God is everywhere' would refuse to apply that statement to filthy places, the opponent's general affirmation of God's lordship collapses when applied to specific evil actions. This lesson unpacks that logical move.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English translation to grasp the structure of the objection and response.
Notice the shift from the verse's ruling to the type of actions.
2
Identify the analogy
The author uses the analogy of 'God is in every place' but not in dirty places. Recognize how this mirrors the opponent's position.
The analogy is central to the refutation.
3
Analyze the logical force
Consider why the inconsistency undermines the opponent's position and what principle is being defended.
Think about the principle of divine lordship and action attribution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم من حَيْده أن سأل عن حكم الآية، فأعرض عن ذلك واشتغل في الإجابة عن نوع الأفعال. وحقيقته أن يقول به في الجملة، وعند التفسير فيما يقبح لا يقول؛ كما يقول: الله في كل مكان؛ فإذا سئل عنه في الحُشُوش والأمكنة القذرة أبي ذلك. ثم هو رب كل شيء وإله كل شيء، ثم عند التفسير فيما يقبح يأبى، إلا أنه لما يقصر بحيث ذلك الإطلاق يدفع أصله، فمثله ما نحن فيه. والله الموفق.
Then from his deflection, that he asked about the ruling of the verse, but he turned away from that and engaged in answering about the type of actions. The truth of the matter is that he affirms it in general terms, but when it comes to interpretation regarding what is ugly/evil, he does not affirm it; just as he says: 'God is in every place'; but when asked about Him in latrines and filthy places, he refuses that. Then He is the Lord of everything and the God of everything, but when it comes to interpretation regarding what is ugly, he refuses, except that when one shortens [the expression] to the extent that that absolute statement repels its own principle, so similar is our case. And God is the Giver of success.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The opponent (likely the Qadariyya) deflects from the actual ruling of the verse and instead discusses the type of actions. The truth is that they affirm the verse in general but when it comes to specific ugly actions they deny it, analogous to saying 'God is everywhere' but refusing to say He is in dirty places. This inconsistency shows that their general affirmation repels their own principle. The argument is that their method is self-defeating.

التفسير
الجملة
الإطلاق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Absolute statements about God (like 'Lord of everything') can be qualified without consequence.
Correction: If a general statement is true, its implications must be accepted consistently; otherwise, the principle is self-contradictory.

D) Saying God is all-powerful but denying miracles

Key Takeaway
Maturidi uses an analogy of 'God is everywhere' to show that an opponent's general affirmation contradicts their specific denial.

Refuting the Qadariyya on 'Allah Created You and What You Do'
Maturidi refutes the Qadariyya interpretation of a key verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Maturidi's argument that the apparent meaning of the verse refers to the creation of human actions, not idols, and his refutation of the Qadariyya's misinterpretation.

Core Idea
The Qur'an's apparent meaning cannot be diverted without clear evidence.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi addresses a key argument from the Qadariyya, who claimed that the verse 'And Allah created you and what you do' (37:96) refers to idols, not human actions. He insists that the apparent meaning is the creation of action and cannot be reinterpreted without proof. He then exposes the logical inconsistency in their position and criticizes their use of another verse to deny the creation of actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's claim
Begin by reading the opponent's interpretation of the verse: that 'what you do' means idols. Notice how they link it to other verses about carving and fabricating.
The opponent is the Qadariyya who denied that Allah creates human actions.
2
Analyze Maturidi's first refutation
Maturidi argues that the apparent meaning is creation of action, and it cannot be diverted without evidence. He points out that the polytheists were rebuked for their actions (carving and worshipping), not merely for the objects.
This establishes that they worshipped their own actions, implying actions are created.
3
Follow the second refutation
Maturidi then criticizes their use of the Bahira verse (5:103) to deny creation of actions, showing that the verse refers to entities (camels), not actions.
This reveals their refusal to accept Allah's report.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider how Maturidi upholds the apparent meaning and uses logical consistency to refute the misinterpretation.
This is a model of kalam argumentation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم احتج لخصمه بقوله: {والله خلقكم وما تعملون} [الصافات 96/37]، قال: يريد به آلهتم كقوله: {أتعبدون ما تنحتون} [الصافات 95/37]، وكقوله: {تلقف ما يأفكون}. قال الشيخ رحمه الله: نقول وبالله التوفيق: ظاهر الآية ذكر خلق العمل، فلم يجز صرف ذلك إلى غيره إلا بالبيان. مع ما في جميع ما ذكر نحتهم داخل، وكذلك إفكهم كما ذكر، وبه عُوبوا لا بذلك الشيء فقط، حيث فعلوا ثم عبدوا، فكأنهم عبدوا فعلهم، فمثله ما نحن فيه. وأيضا إنه لو صُرّح بالآية الهتهم بعد أن ذكر معمولاً، فإذا لم يكن الله خلق العمل لم يجز له القول بخلقه معمولاً، إذ ليس هو كذلك مخلوقاً؛ ثبت أن العمل مخلوق، ليعبدوا مخلوقا معمولاً كما ذكر. ولا قوة إلا بالله. ثم من عظم سفههم أن احتجوا بقوله تعالى: {ما جعل الله من بحيرة} الآية، وتلك أسماء تلك الأعيان في نفي خلق الأعمال، بقوله: {ما جعل كذا}. وهن أسماء تلك الأعيان لا الأفعال، وهن مخلوقات لا شك. ثم يرد فيما ذكر العمل بالخلق إلى حقيقة الأعيان ليدفع خلق الأفعال. فهذا يبيّن أن رأيهم أن لا يقبلوا عن الله خبره، ولا يرجعوا في أمر إلى تدبيره. ذلك. والله أسأل العصمة.
Then he argued on behalf of his opponent with His saying: {And Allah created you and what you do} [Saffat 37:96], he said: He means by it your idols, like His saying: {Do you worship what you carve} [Saffat 37:95], and like His saying: {It swallows what they fabricate}. The Shaykh (may Allah have mercy on him) said: We say, and with Allah is success: The apparent meaning of the verse is the mention of the creation of action, so it is not permissible to divert that to something else without evidence. Moreover, all that he mentioned of their carving is included, and likewise their fabrication as mentioned, and they were rebuked for that, not merely for that thing; for they did [it] and then worshipped, so it is as if they worshipped their own action, so similar is our case. And also, if the verse explicitly referred to their idols after mentioning a direct object, then if Allah did not create the action, it would not be permissible for him to say that He created it as an object, since it is not created in that way; it is established that the action is created, so that they worship a created object as mentioned. And there is no power except with Allah. Then among the greatness of their foolishness is that they argued with His saying: {Allah has not made any Bahira} [Ma'idah 5:103] — and those are names of those entities — to negate the creation of actions, by saying: 'He has not made such and such.' And they are names of those entities, not actions, and they are undoubtedly created. Then he redirects the mention of action with creation to the reality of entities to repulse the creation of actions. This shows that their opinion is that they do not accept Allah's report, nor do they refer in any matter to His planning. That is so. And I ask Allah for protection.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage presents an argument from the opponent (the Qadariyya) who interprets the verse 'Allah created you and what you do' as referring to idols, not human actions. Imam Maturidi refutes this: the apparent meaning of the verse is the creation of action, and it cannot be diverted without clear evidence. He points out that the polytheists' carving and worshipping were criticized; they worshipped their own actions. If the action were not created, they would be worshipping something uncreated, but it is established that the action is created. Then he criticizes their use of the 'Bahira' verse to deny creation of actions, arguing that the verse speaks about entities (camels) not actions. This shows their refusal to accept Allah's report.

Key Terms
خلق العمل
ظاهر الآية
الآلهة
نحتم
إفك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Qadariyya believe that 'what you do' in the verse refers to idols, not human actions, and that actions are not created by Allah.
Correction: Imam Maturidi shows that the apparent meaning is creation of action, and the verse cannot be reinterpreted without clear evidence. The polytheists' sin involved their own actions, implying actions are created.

Key Takeaway
Imam Maturidi defends the apparent meaning of the Qur'an and argues that human actions are created by Allah, refuting the Qadariyya misinterpretation.

Refutation of the Objection about Shared Creation
Maturidi responds to the objection that if actions are created, they resemble God's creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Maturidi argues that human actions do not resemble Allah's creation despite both involving origination.

Core Idea
Similarity in origination does not imply resemblance due to differing aspect and meaning.

Maturidi responds to a key objection: if human actions are created, they would look like Allah's creation. He emphasizes that human actions are inherently different—vain and corrupt—while Allah's actions are wise and good. The mere fact of occurring does not create resemblance, just as 'knowing' differs between God and humans.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the objection from the Qur'anic verse and Maturidi's immediate response.
Pay attention to the structure: objection, then multiple layers of answer.
2
Identify the argument layers
Find the three main points Maturidi makes: (1) actions differ in nature, (2) occurrence alone doesn't cause resemblance, (3) even if there's shared meaning, resemblance only in entities.
The third point is nuanced—resemblance in attributes that subsist in entities is possible but not applicable here.
3
Understand the irony
Notice the final sentence: the opponents charge Maturidi with tashbih, but they themselves equate human and divine actions in reality. This is a rhetorical counter.
This highlights the inconsistency in the opponents' position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال: واحتجوا أيضا بقوله: {أم جعلوا الله شركاء خلقوا كخلقه} [الرعد 13/16]، الآية، إنه على قولكم يشبه فعلكم خلقه. فقال: معاذ الله، بل فعلنا عبث وفساد وخضوع وذلة، وفعله حكمة وصواب وتفضل وتطوّل. قال: وليس من حيث الحدث والحدث والخروج من العدم تشابه لاختلاف الجهة، كما لم يكن في عالم وعالم وحي وقادر لاختلاف المعنى. قال: وبعد، فإن فعلنا يخالف فعل الله لعينه. ثم في الإيجاد والإحداث معنى يوجب التشابه، وإنما يجوز ذلك في الأعيان بما يحل فيها. مع ما يعارض بقول جهم حيث قال: في تحقيق الفعل تشابه. ثم قال: العجب من إلزامهم التشبيه بالإحداث، ولم يلزموا أنفسهم فيما فعلوا فعل ربهم في الحقيقة.
He said: And they also argued with His saying: {Or have they set up partners with Allah who create as He creates} [Ra'd 13:16], the verse, that according to your statement, your actions resemble His creation. He said: God forbid! Rather, our actions are vanity, corruption, submission, and humiliation, while His action is wisdom, correctness, favor, and bounty. He said: And there is not, from the perspective of occurrence and occurrence and coming out of non-existence, any resemblance due to the difference of aspect, just as there is not in knowing and knowing, and living and powerful, due to the difference of meaning. He said: And moreover, our action differs from Allah's action in its very essence. Then, in bringing into existence and originating there is a meaning that necessitates resemblance, but that is only permissible in entities due to what subsists in them. Along with what opposes the statement of Jahm, where he said: In the realization of action there is resemblance. Then he said: The wonder is that they impose the charge of resemblance (tashbih) due to origination, and they do not impose upon themselves that they do the action of their Lord in actuality.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The opponents argue that if human actions are created, they would resemble Allah's creation. The response: human actions are different in nature—they are vanity and corruption, while Allah's actions are wisdom. Moreover, the mere fact of occurring or coming from non-existence does not imply resemblance because the aspect (جهة) differs. Just as 'knowing' can describe two beings but with different meanings. The action's essence is different. Even if there is a shared meaning of bringing into existence, resemblance is only in attributes that subsist in entities. The author then notes that the Jahmiyya claim resemblance in action, and it is ironic that the opponents charge others with tashbih while they themselves equate human and divine actions in reality.

Key Terms
تشابه
الإحداث
الحكمة
العبث
الجهة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that similarity in the concept of 'origination' implies literal resemblance between God and creation.
Correction: Maturidi explains that the aspect and meaning differ, preventing any real resemblance. Even if there is a shared concept, it does not entail similarity in essence.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why do human actions not resemble Allah's actions even though both involve origination?
A) Because human actions are voluntary and Allah's are involuntary
B) Because the aspect (جهة) and meaning differ
C) Because human actions are not actually created
D) Because Allah's actions are eternal

Key Takeaway
The mere fact that both human and divine actions involve origination does not make them resemble each other; the aspect and meaning differ fundamentally.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you plan your day or make decisions, do you ever unconsciously assume that your act of choosing is comparable to Allah's will? How does Maturidi's distinction between aspect and essence challenge that subtle arrogance?
?

?
Think of a time you criticized another person's actions harshly. Did you treat their mistake as if it were an offense against absolute wisdom, as if you were judging from a divine perspective? How can Maturidi's contrast between human actions (عبث وفساد) and divine actions (حكمة وصواب) humble you in that moment?

The Kasb Objection: Distinguishing the Acquired Act
Maturidi responds to an objection about distinguishing the acquired act.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's initial response to the objection that the acquired act cannot be distinguished from other acts, and why indistinguishability does not negate divine creation.

Core Idea
Indistinguishability does not disprove divine creation.

In this passage, Maturidi addresses a new objection against the concept of kasb (acquisition). The opponent argues that if the acquired act cannot be distinguished from other acts, then how can it be a separate category? Maturidi begins his answer by pointing out that even if they are indistinguishable, both acts are still created by God. However, the passage cuts off before the full answer is given.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Note the bracketed uncertain phrase.
The OCR detected [ولكان قد] as uncertain.
2
Identify the objection
The opponent questions whether the acquired act can be known from other acts. What is being challenged?
3
Analyze Maturidi's response
Maturidi says if the acts are confused so reality is unknown, it would be established that both are created together. What does this imply?
The answer is incomplete; consider what might follow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم عارض : هل يُعرف به المكتسب من غيره ؟ قال الشيخ رحمه الله : وهي المعارضة إن اشتبه المكتسب لغيره حتى لا يُعرف حقيقة واحد منهما [ولكان قد] ثبت أنهما مخلوقان معا لذلك. وبعد، فإنه ليس على معرفة
Then he objected: Is the acquired act known from other than it? The Shaykh (may God have mercy on him) said: And it is an objection: if the acquired act is confused with other than it so that the reality of neither is known, [and it would have been] established that both are created together for that reason. Afterwards, he is not upon knowledge.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage begins a new objection about the acquired act (muktasab) in human action. The opponent questions whether the acquired act can be distinguished from other acts. Maturidi's answer begins by stating that if the acquired act is confused with other acts so that the reality of neither is known, then it would be established that both are created together. Unfortunately, the text cuts off at the end of the page: 'afterwards, he is not upon knowledge' is incomplete. The argument likely continues to assert that indistinguishability does not affect the fact that both are created by God.

Key Terms

كسب (kasb/acquisition)
خلق (khalq/creation)

Correction: Maturidi states that even if indistinguishable, both acts are created together, so indistinguishability does not prove human autonomy.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Even if acts appear indistinguishable, they are all created by God, so the objection does not undermine divine creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

The Wisdom in the Creation of Evil
Maturidi answers the objection that if God creates good, He also creates evil, and shows the wisdom in it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's response to the objection that if God creates good, He also creates evil, and the wisdom behind the creation of seemingly evil things.

Core Idea
Evils in creation are not truly evil in divine wisdom; they serve as mercy.

Maturidi tackles a classic objection against divine omnipotence: if God creates good, why does He also create evil? An opponent argues that the same logic should apply to disbelief. In this passage, Maturidi explains the crucial distinction between evils like disease, which have wisdom as reminders and deterrents, and disbelief, which has no wisdom because it requires a responsible agent.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Maturidi uses a dialectical style with an imagined opponent.
2
Understand the objection
The opponent says: if God creates harmful things like diseases, then why not also disbelief? Identify this challenge in the text.
3
Examine the first response (al-faqih)
Maturidi, quoting 'the faqih', says the question is only a counterargument. God is not called the Creator of specific evils by their names.
This shows the importance of language and naming in theology.
4
Explore the answer about wisdom
Evils like diseases are not truly evil in wisdom; they are mercy by prompting repentance and deterring sin. Disbelief, however, has no wisdom — it cannot be created without a responsible agent.
5
Follow Abu Mansur's elaboration
Even the creation of an ugly act like disbelief has wise purposes: it leads one to seek God's protection, recognize folly, and know that it does not harm God. Maturidi refutes the notion that an act could exist without an agent.
This reinforces the necessity of human agency and the wisdom in divine creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم احتج عليهم بخلق الشرور والأسقام ، وأن كانت ضارة، وقال: لم لا قلت هذا في الكفر ؟ . قال الفقيه : وهذا سؤال لا يسأله أحد على الابتداء إلا على المعارضة، إذ لم يُسمّ خالق هذه الأشياء بها وجب أن يسمى بخلقه أفعال الخلق بأسمائها ، وهذا نوع ما ليس لغيره فيه فعل الحقيقة، وفي أفعال الشرور ذلك. فأجاب بأن هذه الأشياء ليست بشرور في الحكمة، بل هي رحمة بذكر التوبة وبزجر عن المعصية، والكفر ليس بحكمة بوجه؛ ألا ترى أنه لا يجوز خلقه لا عن أحد، ويجوز في الأول. قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : فالأول ، يقال له في خلق فعل الكفر قبيحا، وهو يذكر من عاينه عظيم فعله، فيفزع إلى الله بالعصمة عنه ثم يذكره حدث الذي منه فيدعوه إلى التوحيد، ثم يُعرف به سفه من منه ذلك وفسقه، وبه يعرف اسمه وعواقبه، ثم يُعرفه أنه لا يضر الصانع. ولا قوة إلا بالله. وقوله : لا يخلقه لا عن أحد ، كلام من لا يعقل ما يقول، وإلا فهو اسم لفعل العبد فكيف يكون ولا عبد ؟ وهذا كمن يقول : التحرك هو زوال الجسم، وهو لا يخلقه دونه فيجب خلقه منه حكمة؛ وعلى ذلك جميع الأعراض وإبانة الخلق. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then he argued against them by the creation of evils and diseases, and although they are harmful, [he said]: 'Why did you not say this about disbelief?' The faqih said: 'This is a question that no one asks initially except as a counterargument, because He is not called the Creator of these things by their names so that He should be called by His creation of the acts of creation by their names. And this is a type in which no one else has true action, and in the acts of evils that is the case.' So he answered that these things are not evils in wisdom, rather they are mercy by mentioning repentance and deterring from sin, while disbelief is not wisdom in any way; do you not see that it is not permissible to create it from no one, and it is permissible in the first [type]. Abu Mansur, may God have mercy on him, said: 'As for the first, it is said to him regarding the creation of the act of disbelief as ugly, and he mentions from those who witness its great effect, so he flees to God for protection from it, then he mentions the event from which it arises, so it calls him to tawhid, then he comes to know through it the foolishness and wickedness of those from whom it originates, and through it he knows its name and consequences, then he comes to know that it does not harm the Maker. And there is no power except with God. And his saying: "He does not create it without anyone" is the speech of one who does not understand what he says; otherwise, it is a name for the act of the servant, so how can it be without a servant? And this is like one who says: "Motion is the removal of the body," and he does not create it without it, so its creation from him is obligatory by wisdom; and similarly all accidents and the bringing to life [or extinction] of creation. And there is no power except with God.'
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage addresses the theodicy problem: if God creates good, He also creates evil. An objector asks why the same reasoning does not apply to disbelief. Maturidi first responds through 'al-faqih' that the question is only a polemic. God is not called the Creator of specific evils by their names, since names like 'killing' belong to servants' actions. The answer is that evils like diseases are not truly evil in divine wisdom; they serve as mercy by prompting repentance and deterring from sin. Disbelief, however, has no wisdom—it cannot be created without a responsible agent. Then Abu Mansur (Maturidi) elaborates: even the creation of an ugly act like disbelief is wise because it leads one to seek God's protection, recognize the folly of the sinner, and know that it does not harm God. He refutes the idea that an act could exist without an agent, using motion as an example: motion cannot be separated from the body; similarly, an act cannot be without a doer. Thus, creating evil acts from the servant is necessary for wisdom, and this applies to all accidents and the creation of life and death.

Key Terms

كفر
حكمة
توبة
عبد
فعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If God creates evil, He must also create disbelief in the same way, because both are actions.
Correction: Maturidi distinguishes: evils like disease are not evil in divine wisdom; they serve as mercy. Disbelief has no wisdom and requires a servant as agent. God creates the act of disbelief from the servant, but the act itself is the servant's earning.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why are evils like diseases not considered evil in wisdom?
A) They are actually good
B) They serve as mercy by prompting repentance and deterring from sin
C) They are the creation of the servant
D) They do not exist

Key Takeaway
Maturidi teaches that evil in creation is not inherently evil in divine wisdom; it serves as mercy, while disbelief has no independent existence without a servant.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a recent hardship you faced. Did you see it as a mercy that could lead you to repentance, or did you resent God for it? How can you change your perspective starting today?
?
When you witness others committing disbelief or sin, does it drive you to seek refuge in God and reflect on your own need for His protection, or do you feel self-righteous? What concrete step can you take to turn that observation into a deeper tawhid?
?
This passage says that evil in creation is not truly evil in divine wisdom. Is there a situation in your life where you have not yet seen the hidden mercy? Pray to God to show you that wisdom, and commit to waiting patiently for it.

The Wisdom Behind God's Creation of Evils and Diseases
Al-Maturidi refutes the objection that God's creating evils implies naming Him with evil names.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Maturidi's argument that God's creation of evils and diseases is not inherently evil but serves wise purposes, such as prompting repentance and deterring sin, and why this does not attribute evil to God.

Core Idea
Evils are not evil in wisdom; they serve mercy through repentance and deterrence.

Al-Maturidi addresses a common objection against divine predestination: if God creates evil acts, does that make Him evil? In this passage, he explains that such acts are not evil in their ultimate wisdom, and that the objection confuses the act with its purpose. The text presents a layered refutation that also explores the nature of disbelief and diseases.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the flow from objection to answer to further commentary.
This passage contains both the objection and the detailed response from al-Maturidi.
2
Identify the objection and initial response
Find where the opponent argues that creating evils would imply naming God with evil names, and note al-Faqih's initial clarification that this is rhetorical opposition.
Al-Faqih says the question is only asked in opposition, not as a genuine inquiry.
3
Understand the main answer
Focus on the statement 'these things are not evils in wisdom, but rather are mercy by mentioning repentance and deterrence from disobedience.' This is the core refutation.
The wisdom behind evils and diseases is to lead people to repentance and warn against sin.
4
Explore Abu Mansur's elaboration
Read Abu Mansur's commentary on the creation of disbelief. See how witnessing an ugly act can lead one to seek refuge in Allah and to tawhid.
He also critiques the opponent's statement about creation without a subject, using the analogy of movement.
5
Reflect on the application to diseases
Consider the final point that diseases cannot be created without a subject, yet they still have wisdom. This reinforces the lesson that apparent evils have divine purposes.
This ties back to the main argument that God's actions are always wise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم احتج عليهم بخلق الشرور والأسقام، وأن كانت ضارة، وقال: لم لا قلت هذا في الكفر؟ قال الفقيه: وهذا سؤال لا يسأله أحد على الابتداء إلا على المعارضة، إذ لم يسم خالق هذه الأشياء بها وجب أن يسمى بخلقه أفعال الخلق بأسمائها، وهذا نوع ما ليس لغيره فيه فعل الحقيقة، وفي أفعال الشرور ذلك. فأجاب بأن هذه الأشياء ليست بشرور في الحكمة، بل هي رحمة بذكر التوبة وبزجر عن المعصية، والكفر ليس بحكمة بوجه؛ ألا ترى أنه لا يجوز خلقه لا عن أحد، ويجوز في الأول. قال أبو منصور رحمه الله: فالأول يقال له في خلق فعل الكفر قبيحا، وهو يذكر من عاينه عظيم فعله، فيفزع إلى الله بالعصمة عنه ثم يذكره حدث الذي منه فيدعوه إلى التوحيد، ثم يعرف به سفه من منه ذلك وفسقه، وبه يعرف اسمه وعواقبه، ثم يعرفه أنه لا يضر الصانع. ولا قوة إلا بالله. وقوله: لا يخلقه لا عن أحد، كلام من لا يعقل ما يقول، وإلا فهو اسم لفعل العبد فكيف يكون ولا عبد؟ وهذا كمن يقول: التحرك هو زوال الجسم، وهو لا يخلقه دونه فيجب خلقه منه حكمة؛ وعلى ذلك جميع الأعراض وإبانة الخلق. ولا قوة إلا بالله. ثم الأسقام لا يجوز أن يخلقها لا في أحد ولا لأحد، ثم لم يمنع تحقق الحكمة لها، فمثله الذي ذكر. والله الموفق.
Then he argued against them by the creation of evils and diseases, even though they are harmful, and said: 'Why did you not say this concerning disbelief?' Al-Faqih said: 'This is a question that no one asks initially except by way of opposition, since the Creator of these things is not named by them, so it must be that He is named by His creation of the acts of the servants by their names, and this is a type for which there is no real action for other than Him, and that is the case in acts of evil.' So he answered that these things are not evils in wisdom, but rather are mercy by mentioning repentance and by deterrence from disobedience, while disbelief is not wisdom in any way; do you not see that it is not permissible for Him to create it not from anyone, and it is permissible in the first [case]. Abu Mansur, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'The first [point] is said to him regarding the creation of the act of disbelief as ugly, and he mentions from one who witnesses it the greatness of his act, so he flees to Allah for protection from it, then he mentions the event from which it [arose], and it calls him to tawhid (monotheism), then he comes to know the folly of the one from whom that [act] came and his corruption, and by it he knows His name and its consequences, then he informs him that it does not harm the Maker. And there is no power except with Allah.' And His saying: 'He does not create it not from anyone,' is the speech of one who does not understand what he says, otherwise it is a name for the act of the servant, so how can it be while there is no servant? And this is like one who says: movement is the removal of the body, and He does not create it without it, so His creating it from Him is necessary as wisdom; and the same applies to all accidents and the clarification of creation. And there is no power except with Allah. Then diseases are not permissible to be created in anyone or for anyone, yet this does not prevent the realization of wisdom for them, so the like of that which was mentioned [applies]. And Allah is the Granter of success.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer followed by an explanatory commentary from Abu Mansur al-Maturidi. The opponent argues that if God creates evils and diseases, then just as He is called the Creator of those evils, He should also be called by the names of the evil acts He creates in the servants—e.g., He should be called the Creator of murder and theft. Al-Faqih responds that this objection is only raised as a rhetorical opposition, because in reality the Creator is not named by the names of His creations. Rather, He is named by His attribute of creation itself. The acts of evil, when considered as created actions, are not attributed to God in a way that entails naming Him with their names. Then the answer is given that these things (evils and diseases) are not inherently evil in divine wisdom; they serve purposes such as prompting repentance and deterring sin. Disbelief, on the other hand, has no wisdom whatsoever. It is not permissible to create disbelief without any subject, whereas diseases can be created in someone for a wise purpose. Abu Mansur elaborates: regarding the creation of an ugly act of disbelief, the one who witnesses its greatness is led to seek refuge in Allah and is turned towards tawhid. This demonstrates the folly and sinfulness of the person committing disbelief. The servant learns that the act does not harm the Creator. Then Abu Mansur critiques the opponent's statement 'He does not create it not from anyone' as nonsense, because the act is only the act of a servant; how can it exist without a doer? He gives an analogy: someone says movement is the removal of the body, and if movement is not created without the body, then it must be created from Him – but this reasoning is flawed. The same applies to all accidents and the clarity of creation. Finally, he states that diseases cannot be created in no one or for no one, yet they are not without wisdom. The same principle applies.

أعراض

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that if God creates evil acts, then He is evil or should be called by evil names.
Correction: Al-Maturidi explains that God's creation of evils is not evil in wisdom; these things serve good purposes like repentance and deterrence. God is not named by His creations.

Checkpoint
What is the wisdom behind God creating evils and diseases according to al-Maturidi?
A) They are punishments for sinners.
B) They serve as mercy by prompting repentance and deterring sin.
C) They are random and meaningless.
D) They are created by humans.

Key Takeaway
God's creation of evils and diseases is not evil; they serve higher purposes like prompting repentance and deterring sin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a painful illness or a difficult trial, do you truly believe it is a mercy from Allah designed to turn you back to Him, or do you complain and doubt His wisdom? What specific trial are you facing right now, and how will you use it to repent and be deterred from sin?
?
The passage says disbelief has no wisdom at all. Think of a time you entertained doubts or felt ingratitude. That was pure evil with no excuse. What will you do right now to strengthen your faith so that you never fall into that state?
?
Abu Mansur says that witnessing a great ugly act should make you flee to Allah for protection. When was the last time you saw a major sin committed? Did it drive you closer to Allah, or did it desensitize you? Commit to turning every such witness into a moment of seeking refuge and increasing your taqwa.

Refuting the Claim that Inability Indicates Non-Agency
Initial refutation and dialogue on preventing aspects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Qadari argument from inability is logically flawed and how Maturidi uses a counterexample and dialogue to refute it.

Core Idea
Inability does not prove an action is not ours; it can prove the opposite.

The Qadariyya argued that if a person is unable to do a second action while doing a first, that inability shows the first action is not from the person. Maturidi begins his refutation by turning their logic against them and then engaging in a structured dialogue about the preventing aspects. This lesson unpacks that initial exchange.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the logical structure: counterexample, then a question-and-answer format.
Maturidi uses a reductio ad absurdum in the first sentence.
2
Identify the counterexample
Find where Maturidi says that if inability proved non-agency, then inability to do a better action would imply the first belongs to God. Understand why this destroys the Qadari position.
The Qadari would deny that God is the agent of their actions.
3
Follow the dialogue on preventing aspects
Maturidi asks whether the aspects preventing a second action exist. Follow the two branches: if no, the Qadari admits everything is from God; if yes, the argument about equality of ability backfires.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فعلك لم يدل العجز على أنا لم نفعل. ولو كان العجز يدل على ما ذكروا لكان الثاني إذا كان أحسن، فدل أن الأول له. ثم عارض أنه ما يمنعه؟ فقال: لأنا نفعل بآلة وقدرة وعلاج وفكر، ولا تستوى هذه، ولو استوت أمكننا ذلك. فيقال له: الوجوه التي تمنعك هل هي أو لا؟ فإن قال: لا، أعظم القول أن علاجه وفكره ونحو ذلك كان من الله، وهو الذي به أنكر خلق ذلك، فقد أقر به. وإن قال: بلى، قيل: السؤال عن ذلك كله هو أن القدرية زعمت أن الله لو أبقاها، وقد أبقاها للفعل، وكل ذلك أفعال لها القدرة، فما بالها لم تستو، وقد قصدت أن تستوى، وكانت لك القدرة؟ فهذا يبيّن أنه على غير تقديرك يخرج. وما ذكر من المعنى هو الدليل الواضح بأن قد يخرج أحسن من الأول وأسوى على قصد الاستواء على أن ذلك كان كذلك لا به. مع ما لا يبلغ علم أحد إلى تقدير حركته من الهواء والمكان ومن ارتفاع اليد وانخفاضها لو اجتهد كل الجهد والفعل لا يخلو عنه، ثبت أنه لغيره من هذا الوجه. ولا قوة إلا بالله. وعلى ذلك لا أحد يقصد قصد تقبيح الفعل، وقد يكون كذلك، ثبت أنه من ذلك الوجه ليس له. ولو جاز وقوع فعل من وجه لا يعلمه ولا يريده ـ ولو اجتهد كل جهده ليعرف حده ومبلغه ويكون له على ما هو عليه ذلك الفعل - لجاز مثله في جميع العالم وآيات الرسل وغيرها. والقول في المصور هو القول في الفاعل، وفي الصورة هو القول في الفعل، لا فرق بينهما. ثم قوله: «لو أبقى الله القوة / ومن مذهبه أن القوة لا تبقى وقوتين لا معنى له. ثم ما عارض من الفعل فهو يختاره ويعلم ما يفعله ويقصده فهو من ذلك الوجه له»، وقد بينا في ذلك ما ليس هو بعالم بذلك الوجه. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Your action: inability does not indicate that we did not do it. And if inability indicated what they mentioned, then the second action—if it were better—would indicate that the first belongs to him. Then he objected: what prevents him? He said: because we act with an instrument, power, treatment, and thought, and these are not equal; if they were equal, we could do that. So it is said to him: Are the aspects that prevent you (existent) or not? If he says: No, he magnifies the statement that his treatment, thought, and the like are from God, and it is by that that he denied the creation of that—so he has affirmed it. And if he says: Yes, it is said: The question about all that is that the Qadariyya claimed that if God had preserved it—and He has preserved it for the action—and all that are actions that have power, why are they not equal, when you intended equality, and you had the power? This shows that it emerges contrary to your estimation. And what has been mentioned of the meaning is the clear proof that something better and more equal than the first may emerge with the intention of equality, but that it was so not by means of it. Along with that, no one's knowledge reaches the estimation of his motion from air and place and the raising and lowering of the hand, even if he strives with all effort; and the action is not free from it. It is established that it is from something else in this respect. And there is no power except with God. And likewise, no one intends to make an action ugly, and it may be such; it is established that in that respect it is not his. And if it were permissible for an action to occur from a respect he does not know or intend—even if he strives with all his effort to know its limit and extent and it becomes his as it is—then the like would be permissible in the entire world and the signs of the messengers and other things. And the statement about the shaper is the statement about the agent, and about the form is the statement about the action; there is no difference between them. Then his statement: 'If God preserved the power / and his doctrine is that power does not last two moments, it has no meaning. Then whatever action he opposes, he chooses it and knows what he does and intends it, so it is his in that respect,' and we have shown in that what he is not knowledgeable in that respect. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a Qadari argument. The Qadariyya claimed that if a person is unable to perform a second action while doing a first, that inability proves the first action is not from the person but from God. Maturidi refutes this by several points. First, if inability proved that, then the inability to do a better second action would imply the first action belongs to someone else (God), which they deny. Second, they claim that the ability differs due to instruments and thought; but Maturidi asks whether the preventing aspects exist or not. If they do not, then the Qadari has admitted that everything—including thought and treatment—comes from God, contradicting his denial. If they do exist, then the Qadari's claim that God preserved the ability for action is turned against him: why is the ability not equal? This shows that actions are not entirely within human power. Further, no one can fully know or control all the conditions of an action (like air, place, motion), proving the action depends on another (God). Maturidi also argues that if an action could occur without the agent's knowledge or intention, absurd consequences would follow in all actions and miracles. He concludes by equating the shaper and the agent, and the form and the action, and dismisses the claim that power (qudra) lasts only two moments. Finally, he reiterates that we have shown the Qadari is not knowledgeable in that respect.

Key Terms
العجز
الفعل
الآلة
القدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Inability to perform two actions simultaneously proves that the first action is not from the person.
Correction: Inability can be a sign of limited human capacity, not that the action is divinely caused; the Qadari argument leads to contradiction.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what follows if inability indicated that an action is not from the person?
A) The second action, if better, would indicate the first belongs to God.
B) The action would be impossible.
C) The person would be excused from responsibility.
D) The action would be attributed to chance.

Key Takeaway
The Qadari argument from inability is self-defeating; it can be turned against them by showing it would attribute actions to God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever excused yourself from a duty by saying 'I couldn't help it'? How does Maturidi's refutation challenge your tendency to use inability as an excuse for avoiding accountability? What will you do the next time you feel unable to fulfill a responsibility?
?
When you fail to do something you intended, do you blame your circumstances or yourself? This lesson shows that the Qadari argument from inability is self-defeating. How might you be using the same flawed logic to avoid taking responsibility for your actions? Commit to one specific area where you will stop blaming limitations and start seeking solutions.
?
Reflect on a moment you used the excuse 'I didn't have the ability' to avoid a better action. Based on this lesson, what does your inability really say about your agency? Will you now see it as a challenge to seek more effort, rather than a proof that you are not responsible? Write down one step you will take this week to overcome a perceived inability.

Actions Depend on Conditions Beyond Human Control
Argument from lack of control over action conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi argues that actions cannot be entirely from humans because no one has full control over all necessary conditions like air, place, and motion.

Core Idea
No one fully knows or controls the conditions of their own actions.

Maturidi continues his refutation by pointing out that every action involves countless factors—like air, place, and bodily motions—that lie beyond human estimation and control. Even if a person strives, they cannot fully account for these. This shows that actions depend on something else, namely God. This lesson explores that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the core claim
Read the Arabic and translation. Look for the phrase 'لا يبلغ علم أحد إلى تقدير حركته من الهواء والمكان' which is the key claim.
2
Understand the meaning of 'estimation' (taqdīr)
Maturidi says no one's knowledge reaches the estimation of their motion from air, place, raising/lowering the hand. Reflect on what this means for human agency.
Taqdīr here means precise measurement or control.
3
Connect to the conclusion: 'it is from another'
Since the action cannot be free from these unknown conditions, Maturidi concludes it is from something else (God). Trace the logical link.
4
Consider the argument about intention and ugliness
Maturidi adds that no one intends to make an action ugly, yet it may be ugly. This shows actions are not entirely under human intention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Your action: inability does not indicate that we did not do it. And if inability indicated what they mentioned, then the second action—if it were better—would indicate that the first belongs to him. Then he objected: what prevents him? He said: because we act with an instrument, power, treatment, and thought, and these are not equal; if they were equal, we could do that. So it is said to him: Are the aspects that prevent you (existent) or not? If he says: No, he magnifies the statement that his treatment, thought, and the like are from God, and it is by that that he denied the creation of that—so he has affirmed it. And if he says: Yes, it is said: The question about all that is that the Qadariyya claimed that if God had preserved it—and He has preserved it for the action—and all that are actions that have power, why are they not equal, when you intended equality, and you had the power? This shows that it emerges contrary to your estimation. And what has been mentioned of the meaning is the clear proof that something better and more equal than the first may emerge with the intention of equality, but that it was so not by means of it. Along with that, no one's knowledge reaches the estimation of his motion from air and place and the raising and lowering of the hand, even if he strives with all effort; and the action is not free from it. It is established that it is from something else in this respect. And there is no power except with God. And likewise, no one intends to make an action ugly, and it may be such; it is established that in that respect it is not his. And if it were permissible for an action to occur from a respect he does not know or intend—even if he strives with all his effort to know its limit and extent and it becomes his as it is—then the like would be permissible in the entire world and the signs of the messengers and other things. And the statement about the shaper is the statement about the agent, and about the form is the statement about the action; there is no difference between them. Then his statement: 'If God preserved the power / and his doctrine is that power does not last two moments, it has no meaning. Then whatever action he opposes, he chooses it and knows what he does and intends it, so it is his in that respect,' and we have shown in that what he is not knowledgeable in that respect. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a Qadari argument. The Qadariyya claimed that if a person is unable to perform a second action while doing a first, that inability proves the first action is not from the person but from God. Maturidi refutes this by several points. First, if inability proved that, then the inability to do a better second action would imply the first action belongs to someone else (God), which they deny. Second, they claim that the ability differs due to instruments and thought; but Maturidi asks whether the preventing aspects exist or not. If they do not, then the Qadari has admitted that everything—including thought and treatment—comes from God, contradicting his denial. If they do exist, then the Qadari's claim that God preserved the ability for action is turned against him: why is the ability not equal? This shows that actions are not entirely within human power. Further, no one can fully know or control all the conditions of an action (like air, place, motion), proving the action depends on another (God). Maturidi also argues that if an action could occur without the agent's knowledge or intention, absurd consequences would follow in all actions and miracles. He concludes by equating the shaper and the agent, and the form and the action, and dismisses the claim that power (qudra) lasts only two moments. Finally, he reiterates that we have shown the Qadari is not knowledgeable in that respect.

Key Terms
التقدير
الهواء
المكان
اليد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does the inability to estimate one's own motion from air and place prove?
A) That actions are from the human.
B) That actions are from something else (God).
C) That actions are random.
D) That humans have no free will.

Key Takeaway
The dependence of actions on unknown and uncontrollable conditions shows they are ultimately from God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You plan your day carefully—time, resources, route—but conditions like traffic, weather, or your own energy are out of your hands. Does this truth make you anxious or reliant on God? What would it look like to start your next task with 'lā ḥawla wa lā quwwata illā billāh' not as a mere phrase but as a real confession of dependence?
?
Think of a time you harshly judged someone's action as ugly or wrong. Did you know all the conditions they faced? Maturidi says ugliness can arise from factors beyond anyone's control. When will you next pause before condemning—and what will it cost you to withhold that judgment?
?
If your actions are not fully your own, then your successes are gifts and your failures are not entirely your fault. Does that comfort you or disturb you? How does this reshape your gratitude for good deeds and your repentance for bad ones?

Absurdity of Action Without Knowledge and Final Points
Absurdity argument and concluding points on shaper, agent, and power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the absurdity argument if actions could occur without the agent's knowledge, and his closing points on shaper/agent and the Qadari view on power.

Core Idea
If actions could happen without knowledge, then all events would be permissible, including miracles.

Maturidi delivers a powerful reductio ad absurdum: if an action could occur from a respect the agent does not know or intend, then the same would be possible for all events, including the signs of prophets. He then equates the shaper with the agent and dismisses the Qadari claim that power lasts only two moments. This lesson concludes the refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the absurdity argument
Read the sentence beginning with 'ولو جاز'. Notice that Maturidi says if an action could occur from an unknown or unintended respect, then the same would be permissible for all world events and miracles.
This is a logical extension to show the Qadari position leads to chaos.
2
Examine the equation of shaper and agent
Maturidi states that the statement about the shaper (musawwir) is like the statement about the agent, and the form (sura) is like the action. Understand why this is relevant to the argument.
It ties together creation and action.
3
Understand the dismissal of the Qadari view on power
Maturidi rejects the claim that power lasts only two moments and says the Qadari's assertion that they choose and know their action is insufficient because they are not truly knowledgeable in that respect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فعلك لم يدل العجز على أنا لم نفعل. ولو كان العجز يدل على ما ذكروا لكان الثاني إذا كان أحسن، فدل أن الأول له. ثم عارض أنه ما يمنعه؟ فقال: لأنا نفعل بآلة وقدرة وعلاج وفكر، ولا تستوى هذه، ولو استوت أمكننا ذلك. فيقال له: الوجوه التي تمنعك هل هي أو لا؟ فإن قال: لا، أعظم القول أن علاجه وفكره ونحو ذلك كان من الله، وهو الذي به أنكر خلق ذلك، فقد أقر به. وإن قال: بلى، قيل: السؤال عن ذلك كله هو أن القدرية زعمت أن الله لو أبقاها، وقد أبقاها للفعل، وكل ذلك أفعال لها القدرة، فما بالها لم تستو، وقد قصدت أن تستوى، وكانت لك القدرة؟ فهذا يبيّن أنه على غير تقديرك يخرج. وما ذكر من المعنى هو الدليل الواضح بأن قد يخرج أحسن من الأول وأسوى على قصد الاستواء على أن ذلك كان كذلك لا به. مع ما لا يبلغ علم أحد إلى تقدير حركته من الهواء والمكان ومن ارتفاع اليد وانخفاضها لو اجتهد كل الجهد والفعل لا يخلو عنه، ثبت أنه لغيره من هذا الوجه. ولا قوة إلا بالله. وعلى ذلك لا أحد يقصد قصد تقبيح الفعل، وقد يكون كذلك، ثبت أنه من ذلك الوجه ليس له. ولو جاز وقوع فعل من وجه لا يعلمه ولا يريده ـ ولو اجتهد كل جهده ليعرف حده ومبلغه ويكون له على ما هو عليه ذلك الفعل - لجاز مثله في جميع العالم وآيات الرسل وغيرها. والقول في المصور هو القول في الفاعل، وفي الصورة هو القول في الفعل، لا فرق بينهما. ثم قوله: «لو أبقى الله القوة / ومن مذهبه أن القوة لا تبقى وقوتين لا معنى له. ثم ما عارض من الفعل فهو يختاره ويعلم ما يفعله ويقصده فهو من ذلك الوجه له»، وقد بينا في ذلك ما ليس هو بعالم بذلك الوجه. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Your action: inability does not indicate that we did not do it. And if inability indicated what they mentioned, then the second action—if it were better—would indicate that the first belongs to him. Then he objected: what prevents him? He said: because we act with an instrument, power, treatment, and thought, and these are not equal; if they were equal, we could do that. So it is said to him: Are the aspects that prevent you (existent) or not? Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Humans can fully know and intend every aspect of their actions.
Correction: No one can know all aspects, and if actions could occur without that knowledge, absurd consequences follow.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi say would follow if it were permissible for an action to occur from a respect the agent does not know or intend?

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you plan an action, do you ever pause to consider that there are 'respects' (wujuh) of that action beyond your knowledge and intention? How does that awareness change your dependence on God in that moment?
?
Maturidi argues that if actions could occur from an unknown respect, nothing would distinguish prophetic miracles from ordinary events. Reflect on a time you dismissed something as 'random'. Could your assumption have blinded you to a sign from God?
?
The passage says there is no difference between the shaper (muṣawwir) and the agent (fāʿil). In what area of your life do you most resist seeing yourself as being shaped moment by moment, and instead insist you are the sole architect? What small surrender can you practice today?

The Argument from Divine Knowledge
Maturidi argues from Surah al-Mulk that Allah's knowledge of speech implies He creates it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses Surah al-Mulk 67:13-14 to prove that all speech is created by Allah.

Core Idea
If Allah knows all speech, He must be its Creator.

Maturidi begins his scriptural proof with a powerful argument from divine omniscience. He quotes a verse that connects God's knowledge of what is concealed and revealed to His act of creation. This lesson unpacks that logic step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and its translation
Read the Arabic verse from Surah al-Mulk and its literal translation. Notice that the verse links knowledge and creation.
The verse is: {And conceal your speech or declare it; indeed, He is Knower of that within the breasts. Does He who created not know?}
2
Follow Maturidi's reasoning
Maturidi argues: If Allah were not the Creator of what is spoken, He could not use His knowledge of it as proof. Consider why that is.
He says: 'For if He were not the Creator... He would not have argued thereby for His knowledge.'
3
Understand the implication
The argument implies that the act of speaking (voicing or concealing) is itself created by Allah. Otherwise, ignorance could be attributed to the speaker.
Maturidi notes: 'And it is known that ignorance is possible from other than the one who does it.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الدليل عندنا من طريق القرآن على لزوم القول بخلق الأفعال قوله: ﴿وأسروا قولكم أو اجهروا به إنه عليم بذات الصدور ألا يعلم من خلق وهو اللطيف الخبير﴾، فلو لم يكن جل ثناؤه خالقا لما يُجهر ويُخفى لم يكن ليحتج به على علمه. ومعلوم جواز الجهل من غير الذي يفعله، فإذا لم يكن للاحتجاج بفعل سواه معنى: وأيضاً إن الله تعالى قال: هو الذي يسيّركم في البر والبحر، الآية، وقال في موضع آخر: وقدرنا فيها السير سيروا فيها ليالي، الآية، أخبر أن تقدير السير والتسيير فعله، وبه كان السير ومن كان يسير. وقال: ومن آياته أن خلق لكم من أنفسكم أزواجا، الآية، فيها خبر أن جعل المودة والرحمة من آياته، وأن منامكم من آياته وابتغاءكم من فضله من آياته. ومن البعيد إنشاء غيره له من الآيات؛ إذ ذلك الفاعل أحق أن تكون الآية له، وهن كلهن أفعال الخلق. وقال: وجعلنا في قلوب الذين اتبعوه رأفة ورحمة الآية، وقال: أولئك كتب في قلوبهم الإيمان الآية، وقال: وجعل لكم من جلود الأنعام بيوتا الآية، وقال: وجعلنا قلوبهم قاسية. وفي الجملة قال الله: فعّال لما يريد، وفي أفعال العباد ما يريد، وقد وعد أن يفعل ما يريد. وقد ذم الله من أحب أن يُحمد على ما لم يفعل.
Then the proof in our view from the way of the Qur'an for the necessity of affirming the creation of actions is His statement: {And conceal your speech or declare it; indeed, He is Knower of that within the breasts. Does He who created not know, while He is the Subtle, the Aware?} [67:13-14]. For if He, exalted, were not the Creator of what is voiced and what is concealed, He would not have argued thereby for His knowledge. And it is known that ignorance is possible from other than the one who does it. So if there is no meaning in arguing by an action other than His. And also, Allah the Exalted said: {It is He who conveys you on land and sea} [10:22], the verse. And He said in another place: {And We ordained in it journeys; travel therein nights} [34:18], the verse; He informed that the determination of the journey and the conveyance are His act, and by it were the journey and the one who journeys. And He said: {And of His signs is that He created for you from yourselves mates} [30:21], the verse; in it is the news that making love and mercy is of His signs, and that your sleep is of His signs and your seeking of His bounty is of His signs. And it is far-fetched for other than Him to originate these signs; for that agent is more worthy that the sign be his, and they are all actions of the creatures. And He said: {And We placed in the hearts of those who followed him compassion and mercy} [57:27], the verse; and He said: {Those—He has inscribed faith in their hearts} [58:22], the verse; and He said: {And He made for you from the skins of cattle houses} [16:80], the verse; and He said: {And We made their hearts hard} [5:13]. And in summary, Allah said: {Doer of whatever He wills} [11:107; 85:16], and in the actions of the servants is what He wills, and He has promised to do what He wills. And Allah has condemned those who love to be praised for what they have not done.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage is a scriptural proof (al-dalīl al-samʿī) for the doctrine that all human actions are created by Allah. Maturidi presents several Qur'anic verses. First, Surah al-Mulk 67:13-14 argues that Allah knows all secrets because He creates them; if He were not the Creator of what is spoken, He could not use that knowledge as proof. Second, verses about conveying on land and sea (Yunus 10:22) and determining journeys (Saba 34:18) show that the determination and conveyance are Allah's acts, implying human motion is by His creation. Third, signs like creating spouses, love, mercy, sleep, and seeking bounty (Surah al-Rum 30:21-23) are attributed to Allah, yet they are actions of creatures; thus He is the Creator of those acts. Fourth, verses about placing compassion in hearts (al-Hadid 57:27), inscribing faith (al-Mujadila 58:22), making houses from skins (al-Nahl 16:80), and making hearts hard (al-Ma'ida 5:13) all attribute human interior states to Allah's direct action. Finally, Maturidi cites the general attribute 'Doer of whatever He wills' (Hud 11:107, al-Buruj 85:16) and notes that Allah wills actions of servants and condemns those who claim credit for what they did not do—implying that all actions are ultimately from Him.

Key Terms
خلق الأفعال
الدليل السمعي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Allah's knowledge is merely observational, not causal.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the verse itself argues from creation to knowledge, implying that Allah's knowledge is based on His creative act.

Checkpoint
What is the core logic of Maturidi's argument from Surah al-Mulk?
A) Allah knows all things because He is all-seeing.
B) Allah's knowledge of speech proves He created that speech.
C) Human speech is not created because it is voluntary.
D) The verse only refers to angels' speech.

Key Takeaway
Allah's knowledge of human speech is evidence that He creates that speech.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you speak, do you realize that your very words are created by Allah? How does this truth change the way you view every conversation you have today? Will you pause before speaking and ask yourself if what you are about to say is worthy of being created by Him?
?
If Allah is the Creator of your speech, then He knows exactly what you will say before you say it. Are you using your tongue to testify to His oneness and greatness, or are you wasting His creation on gossip, lies, or idle talk? What specific step will you take today to bring your speech into obedience to Him?
?
The verse asks 'Does He who created not know?' — it links knowledge to creation. Does your heart tremble at the thought that every word you utter is known to Allah because He brought it into existence? Are you ready to stand before Him and give an account for every word He created through you? What change must you make starting now?

The Argument from Divine Conveyance and Determination
Maturidi quotes verses on travel to prove human movement is created by Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses verses about travel and journey determination to show that human movement is created by Allah.

Core Idea
Conveyance and journey planning are Allah's acts, so human travel is created.

Maturidi next turns to verses that describe Allah as the One who conveys people and determines journeys. These verses attribute the very acts of traveling and moving to Allah's direct action. Let's see how he extracts the proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the two verses
Read the verses from Surah Yunus (10:22) and Surah Saba (34:18). Notice that both attribute motion and journey to Allah.
Verse 1: {It is He who conveys you on land and sea}. Verse 2: {And We ordained in it journeys; travel therein nights}
2
Identify what is attributed to Allah
Maturidi highlights that 'determination of the journey' and 'conveyance' are explicitly Allah's acts.
He says: 'He informed that the determination of the journey and the conveyance are His act.'
3
Realize the implication for human actions
If conveyance is Allah's act, then the human's own movement is included in that act. Thus, human actions are created.
Maturidi adds: 'and by it were the journey and the one who journeys.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
