Commentary
This passage is a scriptural proof (al-dalīl al-samʿī) for the doctrine that all human actions are created by Allah. Maturidi presents several Qur'anic verses. First, Surah al-Mulk 67:13-14 argues that Allah knows all secrets because He creates them; if He were not the Creator of what is spoken, He could not use that knowledge as proof. Second, verses about conveying on land and sea (Yunus 10:22) and determining journeys (Saba 34:18) show that the determination and conveyance are Allah's acts, implying human motion is by His creation. Third, signs like creating spouses, love, mercy, sleep, and seeking bounty (Surah al-Rum 30:21-23) are attributed to Allah, yet they are actions of creatures; thus He is the Creator of those acts. Fourth, verses about placing compassion in hearts (al-Hadid 57:27), inscribing faith (al-Mujadila 58:22), making houses from skins (al-Nahl 16:80), and making hearts hard (al-Ma'ida 5:13) all attribute human interior states to Allah's direct action. Finally, Maturidi cites the general attribute 'Doer of whatever He wills' (Hud 11:107, al-Buruj 85:16) and notes that Allah wills actions of servants and condemns those who claim credit for what they did not do—implying that all actions are ultimately from Him.

Key Terms
التسيير
التقدير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What two actions does Maturidi attribute to Allah in these travel verses?
A) Creating the land and sea
B) Conveyance and determination of journeys
C) Creating ships and camels
D) Guiding and misguiding

Key Takeaway
Allah's acts of conveying and determining journeys prove that human movement is created.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you walk to the kitchen or drive to work, do you ever pause to realize that Allah is the One who conveys you? How would your day change if you consciously acknowledged that every step is created by Him?
?
This passage says that Allah determines the journeys and conveys the travelers. Do you plan your daily movements as if you are in control, or do you submit to the fact that your ability to move is a gift from Allah? What one change can you make today to act on this belief?
?
If your very ability to move is created by Allah, then what about your actions that are sinful? Do you blame Allah or take responsibility? How does this verse challenge the common excuse 'It was just my nature'?

The Argument from Internal States and Signs
Maturidi cites multiple verses on internal states and God's will to prove creation of actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses verses about love, mercy, faith, and other internal states to prove that all human actions are created by Allah.

Core Idea
Love, mercy, faith, and even hardness of heart are placed directly by Allah.

Maturidi now brings a series of verses that describe Allah as the One who creates emotions, faith, and other internal conditions. He also cites a powerful closing argument: 'Doer of whatever He wills' and the condemnation of those who claim credit for what they did not do. Let's explore these cumulative proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the verses on emotions and faith
Read the verses from Surah al-Rum (30:21), al-Hadid (57:27), and al-Mujadila (58:22). Note that love, mercy, and faith are attributed to Allah's action.
E.g., {And of His signs is that He created for you from yourselves mates... and placed between you love and mercy}
2
Read the verses on other states
Also read verses about making hearts hard (5:13) and making houses from skins (16:80). These show that even the capacity to benefit from things is created.
{And We made their hearts hard} and {And He made for you from the skins of cattle houses}
3
Understand the summary argument
Maturidi concludes with Allah's attribute 'Doer of whatever He wills' and notes that He wills actions of servants. Also, people are condemned for wanting credit for what they did not do.
This final point implies that all actions are from Allah; otherwise, claiming credit would be justified.

ثم الدليل عندنا من طريق القرآن على لزوم القول بخلق الأفعال قوله: ﴿وأسروا قولكم أو اجهروا به إنه عليم بذات الصدور ألا يعلم من خلق وهو اللطيف الخبير﴾، فلو لم يكن جل ثناؤه خالقا لما يُجهر ويُخفى لم يكن ليحتج به على علمه. ومعلوم جواز الجهل من غير الذي يفعله، فإذا لم يكن للاحتجاج بفعل سواه معنى: وأيضاً إن الله تعالى قال: هو الذي يسيّركم في البر والبحر، الآية، وقال في موضع آخر: وقدرنا فيها السير سيروا فيها ليالي، الآية، أخبر أن تقدير السير والتسيير فعله، وبه كان السير ومن كان يسير. وقال: ومن آياته أن خلق لكم من أنفسكم أزواجا، الآية، فيها خبر أن جعل المودة والرحمة من آياته، وأن منامكم من آياته وابتغاءكم من فضله من آياته. ومن البعيد إنشاء غيره له من الآيات؛ إذ ذلك الفاعل أحق أن تكون الآية له، وهن كلهن أفعال الخلق. وقال: وجعلنا في قلوب الذين اتبعوه رأفة ورحمة الآية، وقال: أولئك كتب في قلوبهم الإيمان الآية، وقال: وجعل لكم من جلود الأنعام بيوتا الآية، وقال: وجعلنا قلوبهم قاسية. وفي الجملة قال الله: فعّال لما يريد، وفي أفعال العباد ما يريد، وقد وعد أن يفعل ما يريد. وقد ذم الله من أحب أن يُحمد على ما لم يفعل.
Then the proof in our view from the way of the Qur'an for the necessity of affirming the creation of actions is His statement: {And conceal your speech or declare it; indeed, He is Knower of that within the breasts. Does He who created not know, while He is the Subtle, the Aware?} [67:13-14]. For if He, exalted, were not the Creator of what is voiced and what is concealed, He would not have argued thereby for His knowledge. And it is known that ignorance is possible from other than the one who does it. So if there is no meaning in arguing by an action other than His. And also, Allah the Exalted said: {It is He who conveys you on land and sea} [10:22], the verse. And He said in another place: {And We ordained in it journeys; travel therein nights} [34:18], the verse; He informed that the determination of the journey and the conveyance are His act, and by it were the journey and the one who journeys. And He said: {And of His signs is that He created for you from yourselves mates} [30:21], the verse; in it is the news that making love and mercy is of His signs, and that your sleep is of His signs and your seeking of His bounty is of His signs. And it is far-fetched for other than Him to originate these signs; for that agent is more worthy that the sign be his, and they are all actions of the creatures. And He said: {And We placed in the hearts of those who followed him compassion and mercy} [57:27], the verse; and He said: {Those—He has inscribed faith in their hearts} [58:22], the verse; and He said: {And He made for you from the skins of cattle houses} [16:80], the verse; and He said: {And We made their hearts hard} [5:13]. And in summary, Allah said: {Doer of whatever He wills} [11:107; 85:16], and in the actions of the servants is what He wills, and He has promised to do what He wills. And Allah has condemned those who love to be praised for what they have not done.

Commentary
This passage is a scriptural proof (al-dalīl al-samʿī) for the doctrine that all human actions are created by Allah. Maturidi presents several Qur'anic verses. The Foundation of Taklif: Ability of Means and Rational Proofs
Maturidi defines the required ability for obligation and provides two rational proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that religious obligations are based on the availability of means and circumstances, not on actual power, and you will learn the two rational proofs that support this principle.

Core Idea
Obligation depends on means, not on actual power.

Imam Maturidi begins by establishing a foundational principle: when the Quran mentions 'ability' (istita'a) in the context of obligations like Hajj, it refers to the means and circumstances that make the act possible, not the actual power to do it. He shows that there is consensus on this point and then provides two rational proofs to explain why commanding someone without the necessary means is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Maturidi begins by referencing Quranic verses that mention istita'a.
Pay attention to the phrase 'وهذا النوع مما أجمع على أن الخطاب لا يلزم دونه' – this states the consensus.
2
Identify the two rational proofs
Find the two considerations (النظر من وجهين). The first discusses the impossibility of commanding a non-existent cause; the second focuses on the purpose of command and prohibition.
The first proof uses examples like 'See!' when there is no sight.
3
Understand the link to interpretation of burden verses
Maturidi interprets verses like 'Allah does not burden a soul except with what it can bear' as referring to means and circumstances, not the act itself.
This clarifies that 'ability' in these verses means the presence of causes.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

صبرًا ﴾ [الكهف، ٦٧/١٨]، ثم قال: ألم أقل لك إنك لن تستطيع معي صبرا [الكهف، ۷۲/۱۸] ، ثم قال : وذلك تأويل ما لم تسطع عليه صبرا ﴾ [الكهف، ۸۲/۱۸] ، على تحقيق قدرة الأحوال نفاها " إذ زالت الأفعال. وكذلك قوله : فاتقوا الله ما استطعتم ﴾ [التغابن، ١٦/٦٤]، وغير ذلك. ثم الدليل على لزوم الكلفة دون حقيقة هذا النوع من القدرة السمع والعقل. فأما السمع فما أخبرتُ من الآيات على نفي الاستطاعة، ثم الأمر والنهي والتعيير؛ على ذلك إدراك العقل . ثم الذي يوضح هذا أيضاً قوله تعالى : والله على الناس حج البيت من استطاع إليه سبيلاً) [آل عمران ۹۷/۳]. ومعلوم أنه لا سبيل إلى حقيقة الأفعال حتى يجد الزاد والراحلة، ولو كان لا يجب إلا بوجود حقيقة القدرة قدرة الفعل لم يكن ليلزم أحداً ذلك؛ إذ قدرة الأفعال هي التي تحدث على حدوث الأوقات، والحج غير واجب حتى ترد هي، وهي لا ترد إلا بقطع الأسفار ، فيكون له التخلف إذ هو غير واجب. وكذلك أمر الجهاد؛ إذ لو علم أن الذي معه من قوة الأسباب لا يبلغه لم يفرض عليه الخروج. ومعلوم أن قوة الفعل بعد البلوغ ليست معه للحال ، وقد لزمه فرضه حيث عُيّر من قعد وكذلك نجد القيام والصيام ونحو ذلك يكون له الخروج من ذلك بالبدل ، وإن كان قدرة حقيقة الفعل قد توجد بالجهد؛ ثبت أن فرض الأشياء ليس بها، ولكن بالأحوال. وعلى ذلك جميع العبادات، من يعلم أن ليس معه من السبب ما يتم به الصلاة أو الصيام أو الحج لم يُكلّف ابتداء ذلك. ثم كانت قوة الأفعال لا تبقى، وما بها يختم غير موجودة ، والتكليف لازم. وكذلك الزكوات تجب بالأموال والأحوال وإن احتمل أن يتعذر عليه الدفع لأعذار ترد. ولا قوة إلا بالله . وعلى لزوم التكليف دونه . ولا قوة إلا بالله . وعلى ذلك قول شعيب : وإن أريد إلا الإصلاح ما استطعت ﴾ [هود، ۸۸/۱۱]، أثبت تحقيق الذي قال بوجود الاستطاعة. ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم في إثبات القدرة تحقيق المعنى الذي له أَبْطَلَ القول باثنين، وهو أن يقدر كل واحد منهما على نفي ما يريد الآخر إثباته ، أو يُسر أحدهما ما لا يبلغه علم الآخر. فمن أقدر العبد على ما لا يعلم الله أن يكون ، وعلى أن يجعله كاذبًا فيما أخبر به، وعلى أن يتلف ما أراد الله
And the rebuke of the people of hypocrisy regarding what they perceive and know, and that is supported by His saying: 'And whoever among you cannot [find] the means...' [Quran 4:25], and His saying: 'And [due] to Allah from the people is a pilgrimage to the House – for whoever is able to find a way there' [Quran 3:97]. This type [of ability] is what there is consensus that the address is not binding without it, and it is among the abilities by whose absence one is not excused for leaving the act, nor is one addressed without its completion. Upon that is the interpretation of His saying: 'Allah does not burden a soul except [with] what it can bear' [Quran 2:286], and 'Allah does not burden a soul except [with] what He has given it' [Quran 65:7], and His saying: 'And upon the father is their provision and clothing according to what is acceptable. No soul is charged except with what it can bear' [Quran 2:233]; indeed it is mentioned in the context of mentioning causes and circumstances, not the occurrence of acts. And upon that is the statement of all who affirm the act to the servants; it is a consideration from two aspects. One of them is the impossibility of commanding the use of a cause that does not exist – and these are causes – so it is said: 'See' and there is no sight, or 'Stretch your hand' and there is no hand. The second is that command and prohibition are only for demanding gratitude and warning against ingratitude, so it is not conceivable that [an act] is done where no blessing has appeared nor is its recognition within capacity. And there is no power except with Allah. And the evidence for the other ability is His saying: 'And they were not able to hear' [Quran 11:20], and the saying of the companion of Moses: 'Indeed, you will never be able to have patience with me' [Quran 18:67], then he said: 'Did I not say that you would never be able to have patience with me?' [Quran 18:72], then he said: 'That is the interpretation of that about which you could not have patience' [Quran 18:82], affirming the power of circumstances, denying it when acts ceased. And likewise His saying: 'So fear Allah as much as you are able' [Quran 64:16], and other [verses]. Then the evidence for the necessity of obligation without the reality of this type of power is revelation and reason. As for revelation, what I have reported of verses negating ability, then command, prohibition, and rebuke; upon that reason perceives. Then what also clarifies this is His saying: 'And [due] to Allah from the people is a pilgrimage to the House – for whoever is able to find a way there' [Quran 3:97]. And it is known that there is no way to the reality of acts until one finds provision and mount; and if it were not obligatory except with the existence of the reality of power – the power of the act – then it would not be binding on anyone; because the power of acts occurs only with the occurrence of times, and Hajj is not obligatory until it occurs, and it only occurs by traversing journeys, so one would have the excuse to stay behind as it is not obligatory. And likewise the command of jihad; for if one knew that what he has of the power of causes does not enable him to reach [the destination], then going out would not be prescribed for him. And it is known that the power of the act after arrival is not with him at the moment, yet the prescribed duty has become binding on him, since the one who sat back is rebuked. And thus we find that standing, fasting, and the like – one may exit from them with a substitute, even if the power of the reality of the act may be found with effort; it is established that the prescription of things is not by it, but by circumstances. Upon that are all acts of worship; whoever knows that he does not have with him the cause by which prayer, fasting, or Hajj can be completed is not initially obligated for that. Then the powers of acts do not persist, and that by which they are concluded is non-existent, yet the obligation remains binding. And likewise zakat is obligatory by wealth and circumstances even if it is possible that payment becomes difficult due to excuses that occur. And there is no power except with Allah. Upon that is the coming of revelation and the unanimous agreement of tongues in asking Allah for help and strength for what He has commanded of acts of worship; for if [the power] were already present, or worship were to fall due to its absence, then the asking would be an unjust asking, and the command would be ingratitude for the power He has bestowed. It is established by what we have mentioned that obligation is binding without it. And there is no power except with Allah. Upon that is the saying of Shu'ayb: 'I intend only reform as much as I am able' [Quran 11:88]; he affirmed the reality of what he said by the existence of ability. And there is no power except with Allah. Then in affirming power is the realization of the meaning by which the saying of [the proponents of] two [powers?] is invalidated, which is that each one is able to negate what the other wants to affirm, or one conceals what the other's knowledge does not reach. So who empowered the servant over what Allah does not know to be, and over making Him a liar in what He has informed, and over destroying what Allah wanted?
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument by Imam Maturidi defending the view that religious obligation (taklif) is based on the capacity of means and circumstances (asbab wa ahwal), not on the actual power to perform the act (quwwat al-fi'l). The passage begins by referencing Quranic verses that mention ability (istita'a) in the context of Hajj and other obligations, and states that there is consensus that the address (khitab) is not binding without this type of ability—namely, the ability of means. Maturidi then interprets verses like 'Allah does not burden a soul except with what it can bear' as referring to causes and circumstances, not to the occurrence of acts. He supports this with two rational considerations: first, it is impossible to command the use of a non-existent cause, e.g., commanding a blind person to see; second, command and prohibition are for gratitude and warning against ingratitude, which require prior blessings. After mentioning another type of ability (the ability of circumstances) evidenced by verses like 'They were not able to hear' and the story of Moses and al-Khidr, Maturidi states that the proof for obligation without the reality of this type of power comes from revelation (sam') and reason ('aql). He then uses the example of Hajj: the obligation depends on finding provision and mount, not on the actual power to travel, because that power arises only during the journey. Similarly, jihad and other acts like prayer and fasting are obligatory based on means, and if one cannot complete the act, a substitute is accepted. Maturidi points out that acts of worship are required even when the power to complete them may not persist, yet the obligation remains. He further argues that the universal practice of asking Allah for help and strength proves that the required power is not already present; otherwise, such prayer would be unjust. The passage concludes by linking this discussion of ability to the refutation of dualism (probably the doctrine of two creators or two powers), arguing that if the servant had real power independent of Allah, it would imply that the servant could nullify Allah's will or knowledge, which is impossible.

Key Terms
الاستطاعة (al-istitāʿa)
التكليف (al-taklīf)
الأسباب والأحوال (al-asbāb wa al-aḥwāl)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'ability' in the Quran always means the actual power to perform the act.
Correction: Maturidi shows that in many contexts, 'ability' refers to the availability of means and circumstances, not the actual power.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what does the consensus (ijma') say about the type of ability required for obligation?
A) It is the actual power to perform the act.
B) It is the availability of means and circumstances.
C) It is the intention of the servant.
D) It is the knowledge of Allah.

Key Takeaway
Religious obligations are based on the presence of means and circumstances, not on the actual power to perform the act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just learned that Allah only holds you accountable when you have the means. What obligation are you currently ignoring, telling yourself you 'can't' do it, when in fact you have the means? Will you begin it today?
?
The author says commands are for gratitude. Take a moment: what is one blessing you received today that you haven't thanked Allah for through obedience? How will you use that blessing in a commanded act before this day ends?
?
If you cannot 'see' a spiritual truth because you lack the means (like knowledge or a teacher), what have you done to acquire those means? Are you content with ignorance, or will you actively seek the means Allah has placed within your reach?

The Other Ability: Evidence from Revelation and Reason
Maturidi presents the 'other ability' of circumstances and argues that obligation is binding without the power of the act, using revelation and reason.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's concept of the 'other ability' (al-istita'a al-ukhra) and how both revelation and reason prove that obligation does not depend on the actual power to perform the act.

Core Idea
Obligation is binding even without the power of the act, as shown by revelation and reason.

After establishing the ability of means, Maturidi introduces a second type of ability—the ability of circumstances—evidenced by Quranic verses that negate ability in certain contexts. He then argues that the very fact that revelation commands, prohibits, and rebukes, and that reason perceives this, shows that obligation does not require the actual power to perform the act.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the other ability
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on the verses cited for the 'other ability' (al-istita'a al-ukhra).
Verses include 'They were not able to hear' and the story of Moses and al-Khidr.
2
Understand the role of revelation and reason
Maturidi states that the evidence for obligation without actual power comes from revelation (sam') and reason ('aql). Consider how he uses these sources.
Revelation includes the negations of ability, commands, prohibitions, and rebukes. Reason perceives that obligation is based on means.
3
Reflect on the implications
This distinction prevents the conclusion that obligations are impossible or unjust. It shows that Allah's commands are fair and based on what is within reach.

والمعاتبة في أهل النفاق فيما يدركون ويعرفون وأيّد ذلك قوله : ومن لم يستطع منكم طولاً ، وقوله : والله على الناس حج البيت من استطاع إليه سبيلا ﴾ [آل عمران، ۹۷/۳]. وهذا النوع مما أجمع على أن الخطاب لا يلزم دونه، وأنه من الاستطاعات التي لا يُعير من عدمها بترك الفعل ولا يخاطب به دون استكمال. وعلى ذلك تأويل قوله: ولا يكلف الله نفسا إلا وسعها ﴾ [البقرة، ٢٨٦/٢]، و [ لا يكلف الله نفستا] إلا ما آتاها " [الطلاق، ٧/٦٥]، وقوله : وعلى المولود له رزقهن وكسوتهن بالمعروف لا تكلّف نفس إلا وسعها ﴾ [البقرة، ٢٣٣/٢]، الآية؛ إنها مذكورة عند ذكر الأسباب والأحوال دون وقوع الأفعال. وعلى ذلك قول جميع من يحقق للعباد الفعل؛ وهو النظر من وجهين. أحدهما إحالة الأمر باستعمال سبب ليس موجودا ] - وهذه أسباب - فيقال : «أبْصر» ولا بصر، أو «مُدَّ يدك» ولا يد. والثاني أن الأمر والنهي إنما هما في استئداء الشكر وتحذير الكفران، فلا يُحتمل أن يُفعل فيما لم يظهر ثمة نعمة / ولا احتمل معرفتها الوسع. ولا قوة إلا بالله . والدلالة على الاستطاعة الأخرى قوله تعالى: ﴿وما كانوا يستطيعون السمع ، الآية ، وقول صاحب موسى: إنك لن تستطيع معي صبرًا ﴾ [الكهف، ٦٧/١٨]، ثم قال: ألم أقل لك إنك لن تستطيع معي صبرا [الكهف، ۷۲/۱۸] ، ثم قال : وذلك تأويل ما لم تسطع عليه صبرا ﴾ [الكهف، ۸۲/۱۸] ، على تحقيق قدرة الأحوال نفاها " إذ زالت الأفعال. وكذلك قوله : فاتقوا الله ما استطعتم ﴾ [التغابن، ١٦/٦٤]، وغير ذلك. ثم الدليل على لزوم الكلفة دون حقيقة هذا النوع من القدرة السمع والعقل. فأما السمع فما أخبرتُ من الآيات على نفي الاستطاعة، ثم الأمر والنهي والتعيير؛ على ذلك إدراك العقل . ثم الذي يوضح هذا أيضاً قوله تعالى : والله على الناس حج البيت من استطاع إليه سبيلاً) [آل عمران ۹۷/۳]. ومعلوم أنه لا سبيل إلى حقيقة الأفعال حتى يجد الزاد والراحلة، ولو كان لا يجب إلا بوجود حقيقة القدرة قدرة الفعل لم يكن ليلزم أحداً ذلك؛ إذ قدرة الأفعال هي التي تحدث على حدوث الأوقات، والحج غير واجب حتى ترد هي، وهي لا ترد إلا بقطع الأسفار ، فيكون له التخلف إذ هو غير واجب. وكذلك أمر الجهاد؛ إذ لو علم أن الذي معه من قوة الأسباب لا يبلغه لم يفرض عليه الخروج. ومعلوم أن قوة الفعل بعد البلوغ ليست معه للحال ، وقد لزمه فرضه حيث عُيّر من قعد وكذلك نجد القيام والصيام ونحو ذلك يكون له الخروج من ذلك بالبدل ، وإن كان قدرة حقيقة الفعل قد توجد بالجهد؛ ثبت أن فرض الأشياء ليس بها، ولكن بالأحوال. وعلى ذلك جميع العبادات، من يعلم أن ليس معه من السبب ما يتم به الصلاة أو الصيام أو الحج لم يُكلّف ابتداء ذلك. ثم كانت قوة الأفعال لا تبقى، وما بها يختم غير موجودة ، والتكليف لازم. وكذلك الزكوات تجب بالأموال والأحوال وإن احتمل أن يتعذر عليه الدفع لأعذار ترد. ولا قوة إلا بالله . وعلى ذلك مجيء السمع واتفاق الألسن على سؤال المعونة من الله والتقوية على ما أمر من العبادات، فلو كانت هي موجودة أو العبادة تسقط لعدمها كان السؤال سؤال جور والأمرَ بكفران ما أنعم عليه من القوة. ثبت بما ذكرنا لزوم التكليف دونه . ولا قوة إلا بالله . وعلى ذلك قول شعيب : وإن أريد إلا الإصلاح ما استطعت ﴾ [هود، ۸۸/۱۱]، أثبت تحقيق الذي قال بوجود الاستطاعة. ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم في إثبات القدرة تحقيق المعنى الذي له أَبْطَلَ القول باثنين، وهو أن يقدر كل واحد منهما على نفي ما يريد الآخر إثباته ، أو يُسر أحدهما ما لا يبلغه علم الآخر. فمن أقدر العبد على ما لا يعلم الله أن يكون ، وعلى أن يجعله كاذبًا فيما أخبر به، وعلى أن يتلف ما أراد الله
And the rebuke of the people of hypocrisy regarding what they perceive and know, and that is supported by His saying: 'And whoever among you cannot [find] the means...' [Quran 4:25], and His saying: 'And [due] to Allah from the people is a pilgrimage to the House – for whoever is able to find a way there' [Quran 3:97]. This type [of ability] is what there is consensus that the address is not binding without it, and it is among the abilities by whose absence one is not excused for leaving the act, nor is one addressed without its completion. Upon that is the interpretation of His saying: 'Allah does not burden a soul except [with] what it can bear' [Quran 2:286], and 'Allah does not burden a soul except [with] what He has given it' [Quran 65:7], and His saying: 'And upon the father is their provision and clothing according to what is acceptable. No soul is charged except with what it can bear' [Quran 2:233]; indeed it is mentioned in the context of mentioning causes and circumstances, not the occurrence of acts. And upon that is the statement of all who affirm the act to the servants; it is a consideration from two aspects. One of them is the impossibility of commanding the use of a cause that does not exist – and these are causes – so it is said: 'See' and there is no sight, or 'Stretch your hand' and there is no hand. The second is that command and prohibition are only for demanding gratitude and warning against ingratitude, so it is not conceivable that [an act] is done where no blessing has appeared nor is its recognition within capacity. And there is no power except with Allah. And the evidence for the other ability is His saying: 'And they were not able to hear' [Quran 11:20], and the saying of the companion of Moses: 'Indeed, you will never be able to have patience with me' [Quran 18:67], then he said: 'Did I not say that you would never be able to have patience with me?' [Quran 18:72], then he said: 'That is the interpretation of that about which you could not have patience' [Quran 18:82], affirming the power of circumstances, denying it when acts ceased. And likewise His saying: 'So fear Allah as much as you are able' [Quran 64:16], and other [verses]. Then the evidence for the necessity of obligation without the reality of this type of power is revelation and reason. As for revelation, what I have reported of verses negating ability, then command, prohibition, and rebuke; upon that reason perceives. Then what also clarifies this is His saying: 'And [due] to Allah from the people is a pilgrimage to the House – for whoever is able to find a way there' [Quran 3:97]. And it is known that there is no way to the reality of acts until one finds provision and mount; and if it were not obligatory except with the existence of the reality of power – the power of the act – then it would not be binding on anyone; because the power of acts occurs only with the occurrence of times, and Hajj is not obligatory until it occurs, and it only occurs by traversing journeys, so one would have the excuse to stay behind as it is not obligatory. And likewise the command of jihad; for if one knew that what he has of the power of causes does not enable him to reach [the destination], then going out would not be prescribed for him. And it is known that the power of the act after arrival is not with him at the moment, yet the prescribed duty has become binding on him, since the one who sat back is rebuked. And thus we find that standing, fasting, and the like – one may exit from them with a substitute, even if the power of the reality of the act may be found with effort; it is established that the prescription of things is not by it, but by circumstances. Upon that are all acts of worship; whoever knows that he does not have with him the cause by which prayer, fasting, or Hajj can be completed is not initially obligated for that. Then the powers of acts do not persist, and that by which they are concluded is non-existent, yet the obligation remains binding. And likewise zakat is obligatory by wealth and circumstances even if it is possible that payment becomes difficult due to excuses that occur. And there is no power except with Allah. Upon that is the coming of revelation and the unanimous agreement of tongues in asking Allah for help and strength for what He has commanded of acts of worship; for if [the power] were already present, or worship were to fall due to its absence, then the asking would be an unjust asking, and the command would be ingratitude for the power He has bestowed. It is established by what we have mentioned that obligation is binding without it. And there is no power except with Allah. Upon that is the saying of Shu'ayb: 'I intend only reform as much as I am able' [Quran 11:88]; he affirmed the reality of what he said by the existence of ability. And there is no power except with Allah. Then in affirming power is the realization of the meaning by which the saying of [the proponents of] two [powers?] is invalidated, which is that each one is able to negate what the other wants to affirm, or one conceals what the other's knowledge does not reach. So who empowered the servant over what Allah does not know to be, and over making Him a liar in what He has informed, and over destroying what Allah wanted?
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument by Imam Maturidi defending the view that religious obligation (taklif) is based on the capacity of means and circumstances (asbab wa ahwal), not on the actual power to perform the act (quwwat al-fi'l). The passage begins by referencing Quranic verses that mention ability (istita'a) in the context of Hajj and other obligations, and states that there is consensus that the address (khitab) is not binding without this type of ability—namely, the ability of means. Maturidi then interprets verses like 'Allah does not burden a soul except with what it can bear' as referring to causes and circumstances, not to the occurrence of acts. He supports this with two rational considerations: first, it is impossible to command the use of a non-existent cause, e.g., commanding a blind person to see; second, command and prohibition are for gratitude and warning against ingratitude, which require prior blessings. After mentioning another type of ability (the ability of circumstances) evidenced by verses like 'They were not able to hear' and the story of Moses and al-Khidr, Maturidi states that the proof for obligation without the reality of this type of power comes from revelation (sam') and reason ('aql). He then uses the example of Hajj: the obligation depends on finding provision and mount, not on the actual power to travel, because that power arises only during the journey. Similarly, jihad and other acts like prayer and fasting are obligatory based on means, and if one cannot complete the act, a substitute is accepted. Maturidi points out that acts of worship are required even when the power to complete them may not persist, yet the obligation remains. He further argues that the universal practice of asking Allah for help and strength proves that the required power is not already present; otherwise, such prayer would be unjust. The passage concludes by linking this discussion of ability to the refutation of dualism (probably the doctrine of two creators or two powers), arguing that if the servant had real power independent of Allah, it would imply that the servant could nullify Allah's will or knowledge, which is impossible.

Key Terms
الاستطاعة الأخرى (al-istitāʿa al-ukhrā)
السمع (al-samʿ)
العقل (al-ʿaql)
قوة الفعل (quwwat al-fiʿl)

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the evidence for the necessity of obligation without the actual power to perform the act?
A) Only revelation (sam')
B) Only reason ('aql)
C) Both revelation and reason
D) Consensus of the scholars

Key Takeaway
Obligation does not require the actual power to perform the act; it is established by revelation and reason based on means and circumstances.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a command from Allah that seems difficult, do you immediately think you lack the ability, or do you consider the means Allah has given you? How does Maturidi's argument challenge your perception of your own obligation?
?
Are there areas of your life where you have excused yourself from obeying Allah because you felt you did not have the power to change, even though the means (time, health, resources) were present? What would it mean for you to accept that obligation is binding regardless of your feeling of capability?
?
If obligation is based on means rather than actual power, then what excuse will you have on the Day of Judgment for neglecting a command? How does this teaching transform your sense of responsibility?

Divine Decree
advanced
8 min
Examples from Acts of Worship and the Refutation of Dualism
Maturidi illustrates his theory with examples and refutes dualistic notions of independent power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will see how Maturidi applies his theory of obligation to specific acts like Hajj, jihad, prayer, and zakat, and how this leads to the refutation of any notion of independent power in the servant that would rival Allah's power.

Core Idea
Acts like Hajj and jihad are obligated by means, not by the power that arises during the act.

Maturidi now provides concrete examples to illustrate that obligations like Hajj, jihad, prayer, fasting, and zakat are based on the availability of means and circumstances. He shows that if obligation depended on the actual power to perform the act, these obligations would become impractical or unjust. He then concludes by refuting the idea of two independent powers (a dualistic concept), arguing that affirming real power in the servant would lead to contradictions.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the Hajj example
Read how Maturidi uses the verse on Hajj to argue that obligation depends on finding provision and mount, not on the power to travel.
Note that the power of the act (quwwat al-fi'l) arises only during the journey, but the obligation is binding beforehand.
2
Observe the pattern in other acts
See how similar reasoning applies to jihad, prayer, fasting, and zakat. Maturidi notes that even if one cannot complete the act, a substitute is accepted.
For example, if one cannot pray standing, they may pray sitting.
3
Understand the argument from supplication
Maturidi points out that people ask Allah for help and strength in worship. If they already had the power, this request would be unjust.
This reinforces that the power needed is not inherently possessed.
4
Grasp the refutation of dualism
Maturidi concludes that affirming true power in the servant independent of Allah would imply that the servant could negate Allah's will or knowledge, which is impossible.
Thus, the servant's power is always contingent and created by Allah.

[Quran 4:25], and His saying: 'And [due] to Allah from the people is a pilgrimage to the House – for whoever is able to find a way there' [Quran 3:97]. No soul is charged except with what it can bear' [Quran 2:233]; indeed it is mentioned in the context of mentioning causes and circumstances, not the occurrence of acts. And upon that is the statement of all who affirm the act to the servants; it is a consideration from two aspects. The second is that command and prohibition are only for demanding gratitude and warning against ingratitude, so it is not conceivable that [an act] is done where no blessing has appeared nor is its recognition within capacity. [Quran 18:72], then he said: 'That is the interpretation of that about which you could not have patience' [Quran 18:82], affirming the power of circumstances, denying it when acts ceased. As for revelation, what I have reported of verses negating ability, then command, prohibition, and rebuke; upon that reason perceives. Then what also clarifies this is His saying: 'And [due] to Allah from the people is a pilgrimage to the House – for whoever is able to find a way there' [Quran 3:97]. And it is known that there is no way to the reality of acts until one finds provision and mount; and if it were not obligatory except with the existence of the reality of power – the power of the act – then it would not be binding on anyone; because the power of acts occurs only with the occurrence of times, and Hajj is not obligatory until it occurs, and it only occurs by traversing journeys, so one would have the excuse to stay behind as it is not obligatory. And likewise the command of jihad; for if one knew that what he has of the power of causes does not enable him to reach [the destination], then going out would not be prescribed for him. And it is known that the power of the act after arrival is not with him at the moment, yet the prescribed duty has become binding on him, since the one who sat back is rebuked. And thus we find that standing, fasting, and the like – one may exit from them with a substitute, even if the power of the reality of the act may be found with effort; it is established that the prescription of things is not by it, but by circumstances. Upon that are all acts of worship; whoever knows that he does not have with him the cause by which prayer, fasting, or Hajj can be completed is not initially obligated for that. Then the powers of acts do not persist, and that by which they are concluded is non-existent, yet the obligation remains binding. And likewise zakat is obligatory by wealth and circumstances even if it is possible that payment becomes difficult due to excuses that occur. And there is no power except with Allah. Upon that is the coming of revelation and the unanimous agreement of tongues in asking Allah for help and strength for what He has commanded of acts of worship; for if [the power] were already present, or worship were to fall due to its absence, then the asking would be an unjust asking, and the command would be ingratitude for the power He has bestowed. It is established by what we have mentioned that obligation is binding without it. And there is no power except with Allah. Upon that is the saying of Shu'ayb: 'I intend only reform as much as I am able' [Quran 11:88]; he affirmed the reality of what he said by the existence of ability. And there is no power except with Allah. Then in affirming power is the realization of the meaning by which the saying of [the proponents of] two [powers?] is invalidated, which is that each one is able to negate what the other wants to affirm, or one conceals what the other's knowledge does not reach. So who empowered the servant over what Allah does not know to be, and over making Him a liar in what He has informed, and over destroying what Allah wanted?
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument by Imam Maturidi defending the view that religious obligation (taklif) is based on the capacity of means and circumstances (asbab wa ahwal), not on the actual power to perform the act (quwwat al-fi'l). The passage begins by referencing Quranic verses that mention ability (istita'a) in the context of Hajj and other obligations, and states that there is consensus that the address (khitab) is not binding without this type of ability—namely, the ability of means. Maturidi then interprets verses like 'Allah does not burden a soul except with what it can bear' as referring to causes and circumstances, not to the occurrence of acts. He supports this with two rational considerations: first, it is impossible to command the use of a non-existent cause, e.g., commanding a blind person to see; second, command and prohibition are for gratitude and warning against ingratitude, which require prior blessings. After mentioning another type of ability (the ability of circumstances) evidenced by verses like 'They were not able to hear' and the story of Moses and al-Khidr, Maturidi states that the proof for obligation without the reality of this type of power comes from revelation (sam') and reason ('aql). He then uses the example of Hajj: the obligation depends on finding provision and mount, not on the actual power to travel, because that power arises only during the journey. Similarly, jihad and other acts like prayer and fasting are obligatory based on means, and if one cannot complete the act, a substitute is accepted. Maturidi points out that acts of worship are required even when the power to complete them may not persist, yet the obligation remains. He further argues that the universal practice of asking Allah for help and strength proves that the required power is not already present; otherwise, such prayer would be unjust. The passage concludes by linking this discussion of ability to the refutation of dualism (probably the doctrine of two creators or two powers), arguing that if the servant had real power independent of Allah, it would imply that the servant could nullify Allah's will or knowledge, which is impossible.

Key Terms
الحج (al-ḥajj)
الجهاد (al-jihād)
الزكاة (al-zakāh)
البدل (al-badal)
الاستطاعة (al-istitāʿa)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the servant has independent power to perform acts, which would imply multiple creators or powers.
Correction: Maturidi argues that the servant's power is always contingent and created by Allah; affirming independent power leads to contradictions.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why does the obligation of Hajj not depend on the actual power to travel?
A) Because that power arises only during the journey, so the obligation would be delayed indefinitely.
B) Because Hajj is not obligatory at all.
C) Because the power to travel is given by Allah after the journey.
D) Because the verse on Hajj is abrogated.

Key Takeaway
All acts of worship are obligated by the availability of means and circumstances, not by the actual power to perform them, and this understanding upholds divine justice and refutes any notion of independent power in creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself unable to perform an act of worship perfectly, do you use that as an excuse to abandon it, or do you do what you can with the means you have? This lesson says obligations are based on circumstances, not perfect power. Where are you holding back because you think you lack the perfect ability?
?
This lesson points out that asking Allah for help in worship proves we don't already have the power. How often do you pray for strength to do what Allah has commanded, and do you truly rely on Him, or do you depend on your own sense of capability?
?
Maturidi refutes the idea that you have independent power that could contradict Allah's will. Are there areas in your life where you act as if you are in control, forgetting that your ability comes from Allah? What would change if you lived with constant awareness that 'there is no power except with Allah'?

Obligation Based on Circumstances: The Hajj Proof
Maturidi uses the Hajj verse to illustrate obligation by circumstances.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that the obligation of Hajj is based on possessing the means (sabīl) and circumstances, not on the actual capacity to perform the rituals at the time of obligation.

Core Idea
Obligation depends on having the means, not the actual ability.

Maturidi begins by grounding his argument in both revelation and reason. He references verses that negate capacity in a specific sense, then uses the well-known Hajj verse to illustrate that the condition for obligation is 'finding a way' – the external means – not the precise capacity for the act. This lesson unpacks that proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening statement
Notice how Maturidi invokes both revealed texts and intellect. He says the revealed texts negate capacity, and that the intellect also perceives obligation based on circumstances.
2
Examine the Hajj verse
He quotes Quran 3:97 and explains what 'finding a way' means: provisions and a mount. This is the external means, not internal capacity.
3
Understand the reasoning
He argues that if obligation depended on actual capacity (which arises only at the time of the act), then the pilgrimage would never be obligatory, because that capacity does not exist until after traveling. Therefore, obligation is tied to the initial means.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السمع فما أخبرتُ من الآيات على نفي الاستطاعة، ثم الأمر والنهي والتعيير؛ وعلى ذلك إدراك العقل. ثم الذي يوضح هذا أيضاً قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيْهِ سَبِيلًا﴾ [آل عمران 97]. ومعلوم أنه لا سبيل إلى حقيقة الأفعال حتى يجد الزاد والراحلة، ولو كان لا يجب إلا بوجود حقيقة القدرة قدرة الفعل لم يكن ليلزم أحداً ذلك؛ إذ قدرة الأفعال هي التي تحدث على حدوث الأوقات، والحج غير واجب حتى ترد هي، وهي لا ترد إلا بقطع الأسفار، فيكون له التخلف إذ هو غير واجب. وكذلك أمر الجهاد؛ إذ لو علم أن الذي معه من قوة الأسباب لا يبلغه لم يفرض عليه الخروج. ومعلوم أن قوة الفعل بعد البلوغ ليست معه للحال، وقد لزمه فرضه حيث عُيّر من قعد. وكذلك نجد القيام والصيام ونحو ذلك يكون له الخروج من ذلك بالبدل، وإن كان قدرة حقيقة الفعل قد توجد بالجهد؛ ثبت أن فرض الأشياء ليس بها، ولكن بالأحوال. وعلى ذلك جميع العبادات، من يعلم أن ليس معه من السبب ما يتم به الصلاة أو الصيام أو الحج لم يُكلّف ابتداء ذلك. ثم كانت قوة الأفعال لا تبقى، وما بها يختم غير موجودة، والتكليف لازم. وكذلك الزكوات تجب بالأموال والأحوال وإن احتمل أن يتعذر عليه الدفع لأعذار ترد. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
The revealed texts [sam'] have informed us of verses negating capacity [istitā'a], then command and prohibition and blame; and on that is the perception of the intellect. Then that which clarifies this also is His statement, exalted: 'And Allah upon the people is the pilgrimage to the House for whoever finds a way to it' (Quran 3:97). And it is known that there is no way to the reality of actions until one finds provisions and a mount. And if it were not obligatory except with the existence of the reality of capacity—the capacity of the act—then it would not be incumbent upon anyone; for the capacities of acts are those that occur at the occurrence of times, and the pilgrimage is not obligatory until it arrives, and it does not arrive except by traversing journeys, so he would have the option to stay behind since it is not obligatory. And likewise the matter of jihad; for if he knew that what he possesses of the strength of means does not take him to it, going out would not be imposed upon him. And it is known that the strength of the act after arrival is not with him at present, yet the obligation was incumbent upon him despite censure of the one who stayed behind. And likewise we find standing and fasting and the like: he has an exit from that by a substitute, even if the capacity of the reality of the act may exist by effort. It is established that the obligation of things is not by them, but by circumstances. And upon that are all acts of worship: whoever knows that he does not have of the means that by which he could complete the prayer, or fasting, or pilgrimage, is not obligated initially. Then the powers of acts do not persist, and that by which they are ended is non-existent, yet the obligation is binding. And likewise the alms-taxes are obligatory by wealth and circumstances, even if it is possible that payment becomes difficult for him due to excuses that occur. And there is no power except by Allah.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage is an argument establishing that Islamic obligations (taklīf) are not conditional upon the actual existence of the capacity (istitā'a) to perform the act at the moment of obligation. Instead, they are based on the presence of external means (sabab) and general circumstances (aḥwāl). Maturidi begins by referring to revealed texts that negate capacity in some sense, but then explains that the intellect also perceives that obligation is tied to circumstances. He uses the Quranic verse on Hajj to illustrate: the condition for Hajj is finding a way (sabīl), which includes provisions and a mount, not the actual ability to perform all rituals at that moment. If Hajj were only obligatory when the exact capacity for the act exists, then it would never be obligatory because that capacity arises only at the specific times of the rituals, which come only after traveling. So the obligation is based on having the means to undertake the journey. Similarly for jihad: the obligation is based on having the strength of means (quwwat al-asbāb) to reach the battlefield, not on having the capacity for fighting at that moment. He notes that after arrival, the strength for the act is not present (due to fatigue), yet the obligation was still binding. For acts like standing in prayer, a substitute (sitting) is allowed if unable, showing that the obligation is not tied to the exact capacity. He concludes that obligations are fixed by circumstances (aḥwāl), not by actual capacity. He extends this to all worships: if one lacks the means to complete prayer, fasting, or Hajj, he is not initially obligated. Then he states that the powers of acts do not persist and are absent at the moment of obligation, yet obligation remains. Finally, zakat is obligatory based on wealth and circumstances, even if later obstacles arise. The passage ends with the refrain 'There is no power except by Allah'.

Key Terms
استطاعة (capacity)
سبيل (way/means)
قدرة الفعل (capacity for the act)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Islamic obligations are only required if one has the immediate ability to perform the act at the moment of command.
Correction: Maturidi shows with Hajj that the obligation is based on having the means to undertake the journey, not on having the exact capacity for the rituals.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi's argument from Hajj, what is the condition for the obligation of Hajj?
A) The actual ability to perform all rituals
B) Finding provisions and a mount
C) The intention to perform Hajj
D) Prior knowledge of ability

Key Takeaway
The obligation of Hajj depends on having the means to reach Mecca, not on the actual capacity to perform the rituals at that moment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a religious duty you have delayed because you felt you weren't 'ready' or didn't have the immediate ability. In light of this lesson, do you already have the means to begin? What is stopping you from taking the first step today?
?
This lesson teaches that obligation is tied to having the way (sabīl), not the actual capacity. Is there a command of Allah that you have treated as 'not yet required' because you think you cannot do it perfectly right now? How might this lesson correct your hesitation?
?
Reflect on a time you used 'lack of ability' as an excuse to avoid an obligation, when really you had the resources. How does the Hajj example challenge your self-justification? What would it mean to change that pattern today?

Obligation Based on Circumstances: Further Examples
Maturidi provides additional examples to reinforce the principle that obligation depends on circumstances.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi applies the principle of obligation by circumstances to jihad, standing in prayer, fasting, and zakat, confirming that obligations are tied to external means.

Core Idea
All acts of worship are obligatory by circumstances, not by actual capacity.

Maturidi extends the same reasoning to jihad, where the obligation is based on having the strength of means to reach the battlefield, and to acts like standing in prayer, where a substitute is allowed if one cannot stand. He generalizes this to all worship and even to zakat, showing the consistency of his principle.

Guided Path
1
Examine the jihad example
Maturidi says that if one lacks the means to reach the battlefield, jihad is not obligatory. He notes that even after arrival, the strength for fighting is not present, yet the obligation was binding.
2
Consider standing and fasting
For acts requiring standing, a substitute (sitting) is permitted, showing that obligation is not tied to the exact capacity.
3
General principle
He states that obligations are fixed by circumstances (aḥwāl), not by capacities. This applies to all acts of worship.
4
Apply to zakat
Zakat is obligatory based on wealth and circumstances, even if later payment becomes difficult.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السمع فما أخبرتُ من الآيات على نفي الاستطاعة، ثم الأمر والنهي والتعيير؛ وعلى ذلك إدراك العقل. ثم الذي يوضح هذا أيضاً قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيْهِ سَبِيلًا﴾ [آل عمران 97]. ومعلوم أنه لا سبيل إلى حقيقة الأفعال حتى يجد الزاد والراحلة، ولو كان لا يجب إلا بوجود حقيقة القدرة قدرة الفعل لم يكن ليلزم أحداً ذلك؛ إذ قدرة الأفعال هي التي تحدث على حدوث الأوقات، والحج غير واجب حتى ترد هي، وهي لا ترد إلا بقطع الأسفار، فيكون له التخلف إذ هو غير واجب. وكذلك أمر الجهاد؛ إذ لو علم أن الذي معه من قوة الأسباب لا يبلغه لم يفرض عليه الخروج. ومعلوم أن قوة الفعل بعد البلوغ ليست معه للحال، وقد لزمه فرضه حيث عُيّر من قعد. وكذلك نجد القيام والصيام ونحو ذلك يكون له الخروج من ذلك بالبدل، وإن كان قدرة حقيقة الفعل قد توجد بالجهد؛ ثبت أن فرض الأشياء ليس بها، ولكن بالأحوال. وعلى ذلك جميع العبادات، من يعلم أن ليس معه من السبب ما يتم به الصلاة أو الصيام أو الحج لم يُكلّف ابتداء ذلك. ثم كانت قوة الأفعال لا تبقى، وما بها يختم غير موجودة، والتكليف لازم. وكذلك الزكوات تجب بالأموال والأحوال وإن احتمل أن يتعذر عليه الدفع لأعذار ترد. ولا قوة إلا بالله.

According to Maturidi, why is a substitute allowed for standing in prayer?
A) Because capacity is never present
B) Because obligation is based on circumstances, not actual capacity
C) Because standing is not essential

Key Takeaway
All obligations in Islam are determined by the presence of external means and general circumstances, not by the exact capacity to perform the act at that moment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know that prayer is obligatory even when you are tired. But have you ever used tiredness as an excuse to skip or delay prayer, while the Prophet ﷺ himself led prayers while wounded? Where is your sense of obligation when Allah’s command meets your comfort?
?
If obligation depends on circumstances, and Allah knows that you do not have the means, He does not hold you accountable. But reflect: how many times have you had the means—health, wealth, time—yet chose not to act? What does that say about your sincerity?
?
The passage ends with 'There is no power except by Allah.' When you last failed to fulfill an obligation, did you turn to Allah asking for strength, or did you simply ignore it? How would your life change if you truly believed that all power comes from Him?

Asking Divine Aid Proves Capacity is Not Pre-Existent
Maturidi argues that asking Allah for help proves that capacity is not independently possessed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the universal practice of asking Allah for help demonstrates that human capacity is not independently possessed but is granted by Allah at the time of action.

Core Idea
Asking for help proves we do not own capacity; it is a gift.

Maturidi presents a second argument based on the universal human practice of supplication. Both revelation and common speech show that people ask Allah for strength to perform worship. If capacity were already present, such asking would be unjust. This passage unpacks that logic and concludes that capacity comes from Allah at the moment of action.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that Maturidi bases his argument on two things: the universal practice of asking for help (isti'āna) and a Quranic verse. Let the text speak before you analyze.
The passage is short but dense. Read it twice.
2
Examine the core logical argument
Identify the conditional reasoning: 'if capacity existed... then asking would be unjust'. Ask yourself: why would it be unjust? What does that reveal about the nature of capacity?
Maturidi uses a reductio ad absurdum: if capacity were independent, asking would imply either asking for what one already has (unjust) or complaining about a non-existent lack.
3
Connect to the Quranic proof
Read the verse of Shu'ayb (11:88). Maturidi interprets 'as far as I am able' as affirming that capacity is real but dependent on Allah. Notice how the verse reinforces the argument from supplication.
The verse shows that even a prophet acknowledges his limited ability, pointing to divine grant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى ذلك مجيء السمع واتفاق الألسن على سؤال المعونة من الله والتقوية على ما أمر من العبادات، فلو كانت هي موجودة أو العبادة تسقط لعدمها كان السؤال سؤال جور والأمرَ بكفران ما أنعم عليه من القوة. ثبت بما ذكرنا لزوم التكليف دونه. ولا قوة إلا بالله. وعلى ذلك قول شعيب: ﴿وَإِنْ أُرِيدُ إِلَّا الْإِصْلَاحَ مَا اسْتَطَعْتُ﴾ [هود 88]، أثبت تحقيق الذي قال بوجود الاستطاعة. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And upon that is the coming of revelation and the agreement of tongues in asking for assistance from Allah and for strength regarding what He has commanded of acts of worship. For if capacity [i.e., independent ability] existed, or worship fell due to its absence, the asking would be an unjust request and a command to be ungrateful for the strength He has bestowed. It is established by what we have mentioned that obligation is binding without it. And there is no power except by Allah. And upon that is the saying of Shu'ayb: 'And I intend only reform, as far as I am able' (Quran 11:88). He affirmed the reality of what he said by the existence of capacity. And there is no power except by Allah.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage presents a second argument: the universal practice of asking God for help (isti'āna) in performing worship. Maturidi points out that both revelation and common speech agree that people ask God for assistance and strength to fulfill obligations. If humans already possessed an independent capacity to perform acts, or if the obligation would be dropped in its absence, then asking for help would be a request for something unjust (jawr) — essentially asking God to give what He already gave or to complain about a lack that is not real. Moreover, commanding such asking would be tantamount to commanding ingratitude for a capacity He supposedly already granted. Therefore, the very act of supplication proves that capacity is not pre-existent but is rather granted at the time of action. He then cites the Quranic verse where Prophet Shu'ayb says 'as far as I am able' (mā istaṭa'tu), interpreting it as affirming that he has capacity (istitā'a) but in the context of divine assistance, not as an independent power.

Key Terms
سؤال المعونة (asking for help)
استطاعة (capacity)
تكليف (obligation)
شعيب (Shu'ayb)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that asking God for help implies human powerlessness or that capacity is completely absent.
Correction: Maturidi shows that asking demonstrates dependence on God's grant of capacity at the moment of action, not that capacity does not exist. Capacity is real but not independent.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why does the fact that people ask God for strength in worship disprove independent human capacity?
A) Because asking implies a lack, but if capacity were independent, there would be no lack.
B) Because God only hears prayers of those who have no capacity.
C) Because asking for strength is a sign of weakness, not a proof of anything.
D) Because the Quran forbids asking for help if one has capacity.

Key Takeaway
The universal human practice of asking Allah for help proves that capacity is not independently possessed but is a divine grant.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you begin your daily prayers, do you consciously ask Allah for the strength to complete them, or do you rely on your own ability? How would your prayer change if you truly believed that every moment of focus and energy is a direct gift from Him?
?
Think of a time you struggled to fulfill an obligation. Did you turn to Allah in desperation, or did you try to force your own capacity? What does your instinct reveal about what you believe regarding the source of your ability?
?
If you fully internalized that your capacity is not your own but a constant divine grant, what would you do differently in your next act of worship? Would you prepare differently, approach with more humility, or ask more sincerely? Commit to one specific change.

The Dualist Logic Applied to Human Capacity
Maturidi defines the meaning that invalidates dualism and applies it to those who affirm independent human capacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the critique of dualism to expose the contradiction in affirming independent human capacity.

Core Idea
Affirming human capacity makes humans like a second god — able to thwart God's will.

Maturidi begins by recalling the standard refutation of dualism: if there were two gods, each could negate the other's actions. He then applies this same logic to those who affirm independent human capacity, showing that if humans can act independently, they can make God a liar or ignorant — a description incompatible with divinity.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dualist error
Learn why dualism fails: each of two gods would be able to negate what the other wills or bring about what the other does not know.
This is the core argument against dualism.
2
See the parallel to human capacity
Notice that Maturidi argues that if humans have independent power, they can make God a liar, ignorant, or a promise-breaker — exactly the same problem.
Humans would have power over God's attributes.
3
Recognize the conclusion
Understand that such a description negates divinity, so the same reasoning that refutes dualism also refutes affirming independent human capacity.
This refutes the sect that affirms independent human capacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم في إثبات القدرة تحقيق المعنى الذي له أبطَلَ القول باثنين، وهو أن يقدر كل واحد منهما على نفي ما يريد الآخر إثباته، أو يُسر أحدهما ما لا يبلغه علم الآخر. فمن أقدر العبد على ما لا يعلم الله أن يكون، وعلى أن يجعله كاذبًا فيما أخبر به، وعلى أن يتلف ما أراد الله إبقاءه قدر على تسفيه الله وتجهيله وخلفه في الوعد، ومن ذلك وصفه ليس بإله؛ وبمثله نفوا قول الثنوية. مع ما في هذا أمر عجيب أن يكون الله يُقوسى أحدًا على نقض ربوبيته؛ إذ مَلَكَ تصييره كاذبًا وقدر على جعله جاهلاً، وعن وفاء ما وعده عاجزاً. وهذا النوع من الإقدار لا يفعله أسفه السفهاء، فكيف أحكم الحاكمين؟ ولا قوة إلا بالله. وعلى قول هؤلاء يكون للبشر قدرة نقض تدبير العالم، وللرسل قوة أن لا يظهروا الله حجة في الأرض، وأن يمتنع كل منهم عن الوجه الذي عليه مضى تدبير العالم؛ وهو مبنى على كون أحواله على أيدى البشر وخلق الأرض والسماء؛ والله تعالى لم يكن له قدرة على خلق تلك الأفعال والأحوال على أيديهم، ولهم قدرة على أن لا يفعلوا شيئًا من ذلك. فإذا لهم عليه أرفع المنن وأعلى النعم، إذ على القدرة في منع تقديره ونفاذ تدبيره فعلوا الذي به قام تدبيره وتم ملكه وسلطانه على ما دبر وشاء، وذلك أوحش قول وبالله التوفيق.
Then in affirming capacity is the realization of the meaning by which the statement of dualism is invalidated, namely that each one of them [i.e., two gods] would be able to negate what the other wills to affirm, or one of them would bring about what the other's knowledge does not reach. For whoever empowers the servant to do what God does not know to be, and to make Him a liar in what He has informed, and to destroy what God willed to preserve, he has the power to make God foolish, ignorant, and a breaker of His promise, and by that he describes Him as not being God; and by the like of this they negated the statement of the Dualists. Moreover, in this is a wondrous matter: that God should empower someone to nullify His lordship; since he has the power to make Him a liar, ability to make Him ignorant, and inability to fulfill His promise. This type of empowerment is not done by the most foolish of fools, so how could it be done by the wisest of the wise? And there is no power except by Allah. And according to the statement of these [i.e., those who affirm independent capacity], humans would have the power to nullify the governance of the world, and the messengers would have the power not to manifest God's proof on earth, and each of them could refrain from the course upon which the governance of the world proceeded; this is built upon the fact that His affairs are at the hands of humans and the creation of earth and sky; and Allah, exalted, would not have the power to create those acts and states at their hands, while they have the power not to do any of that. Thus they would have upon Him the highest favors and the loftiest blessings, since despite the ability to prevent His decree and the execution of His governance, they did that by which His governance stood and His kingdom and sovereignty were completed over what He decreed and willed. And that is a most hideous saying. And by Allah is success.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of dualism (thnawiyya) by demonstrating that affirming independent human capacity leads to absurd consequences that resemble the dualist error. Maturidi first explains the meaning that invalidates dualism: dualists believe in two eternal principles, each able to negate what the other wills. He then argues that if humans are given independent capacity (qudra) to do what God does not know will happen, to make God a liar, or to destroy what God wills to preserve, then humans have power over God's attributes — making Him foolish, ignorant, and a promise-breaker. Such a description is incompatible with divinity. The dualists were refuted by such arguments. Maturidi then expresses astonishment that anyone could think God would empower a creature to contradict His lordship. He rhetorically asks how the wisest of judges would do what even the most foolish would not do. He then extends the argument: on this view, humans could thwart God's plan for the world, messengers could fail to deliver proofs, and God would be incapable of creating acts through them while they have power to refuse. This would mean humans confer favors on God by choosing to cooperate. Maturidi calls this a most hideous saying.

Key Terms
ثنوية (dualism)
قدرة (capacity/power)
تسفيه الله (making God foolish)
تجهيل الله (making God ignorant)
خلف الوعد (breaking promise)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume that affirming human capacity is a neutral theological position.
Correction: Maturidi shows that it logically leads to describing God as ignorant, liar, and promise-breaker, which is the same error as dualism.

Checkpoint
What is the twofold meaning that invalidates dualism, according to Maturidi?
A) Each god could create the other.
B) Each god could negate the other's will or bring about what the other does not know.
C) Each god could destroy the world.
D) Each god could not coexist.

Key Takeaway
Affirming independent human capacity leads to the same absurd conclusion as dualism: it ascribes to creatures power over God's attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make a decision without consulting God's guidance or considering His will, are you not acting as if you have a power that bypasses His sovereignty? How does this passage expose the hidden shirk in your daily independence?
?
Have you ever justified a sin by saying 'I couldn't help it' or 'it was my choice,' as if your capacity is autonomous? How would Maturidi's argument change that justification?
?
If truly believing that God is the only one with ultimate power would transform every moment of your life, what specific habit or thought pattern must you abandon today to stop 'making God foolish' by your actions?

The Wondrous Absurdity of Empowered Creatures
Maturidi expresses astonishment at the notion of God empowering creatures to nullify His lordship, and draws out absurd consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's rhetorical argument that empowering creatures to contradict God's lordship is absurd and leads to grotesque consequences.

Core Idea
If God empowered humans to thwart Him, God would be less wise than a fool.

Having established that affirming independent human capacity echoes the dualist error, Maturidi now expresses astonishment at the idea itself: that God would empower a creature to nullify His lordship. He then extends the reasoning to show that on this view, messengers could fail to deliver proofs, and humans would hold favors over God. He concludes that this is a most hideous saying.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the rhetorical wonder
Maturidi expresses amazement that God would empower anyone to nullify His lordship — making Him a liar, ignorant, and unable to fulfill promises.
This is an emotional and logical appeal.
2
Consider the parallel with human foolishness
Even the most foolish person would not empower another to undermine them. How then would the Wisest of judges do so?
This highlights the absurdity.
3
Extend the argument to messengers and world governance
If humans have independent power, they could thwart God's plan, and messengers could fail to manifest God's proof. This would mean God is not in control.
The implication extends to prophecy and divine decree.
4
Conclude with the hideous result
On this view, humans would have the highest favors upon God because they chose to obey despite being able to disobey. This is a most hideous saying.
It reverses the relationship between Creator and creature.

?

?
This passage says humans would have the highest favors upon God if they chose to obey after having power to disobey. Do you ever feel that your worship puts God in your debt? What does this passage challenge about that mindset, and how will you change that attitude starting today?
?

Common Usage Shows Capacity Refers to Circumstances
Maturidi argues that everyday speech about 'cannot' refers to circumstantial inability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses everyday language to argue that human capacity is understood as dependent on circumstances, not as an independent power.

Core Idea
Everyday 'I cannot' reveals capacity as circumstantial, not autonomous.

Imam Maturidi turns to common speech to support a theological point. He observes that when people say 'I cannot', they usually refer to external obstacles like work or weight, not a lack of inner ability. This lesson examines his reasoning and its implications for understanding divine power.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once, then the translation. Notice the quoted phrases and the logical flow.
The passage is concise but carries a deep argument.
2
Identify the key examples
Look for the examples Maturidi gives of common speech ('I cannot because of my work', 'I cannot move this'). Consider what they imply about capacity.
These are not random examples; they show how people use language.
3
Follow the argument
Trace Maturidi's reasoning: people speak this way, God would not let them speak falsehood, so their usage reflects a real understanding that capacity is tied to means and circumstances.
This is an argument from linguistic consistency.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Maturidi concludes that behind such expressions, people acknowledge a capacity they mention in excuses for specific actions, not in general statements that might make circumstances seem independent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم وجود هذا القول ظاهر في الخلق: لا أقدر لشغلي بكذا، أو لا أستطيع بنقل هذا على. ولم يجز أن يكون الله ينطق ألسن الخلق على غير تمانع منهم بما هو كذب في الحقيقة، وهم يعلمون أن استطاعة الأسباب والأحوال؛ فثبت أن وراء ذلك عندهم قدرة معهم يذكرونها مع الاعتذار في الأفعال لا في الجمل التي تُرجع الأوهام إلى الأحوال. ولا قوة إلا بالله.
Then the existence of this statement is apparent among people: 'I am not able because of my occupation with such-and-such' or 'I cannot move this.' And it is not permissible that Allah would make the tongues of people speak, without any mutual opposition from them, that which is false in reality, while they know that the capacity is for means and circumstances. So it is established that beyond that they have a capacity with them that they mention with excuse in actions, not in the general statements that return imaginations to circumstances. And there is no power except by Allah.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This passage uses common linguistic usage to support the argument. Maturidi observes that people frequently say 'I am not able because of my work' or 'I cannot carry this' — using 'cannot' to refer to circumstantial impediments (like preoccupation or heaviness), not to an absence of inner capacity. He argues that it is inconceivable that Allah would make people speak falsehood in this way without correction, especially since they themselves know that what they mean is the capacity of means and circumstances (istitā'at al-asbāb wa l-aḥwāl). Thus, behind such expressions, people actually acknowledge a capacity that they mention in excuses for specific actions, but not in general statements that might lead imaginations to attribute power to circumstances alone. This shows that the common understanding of capacity is tied to external factors, not to an independent power in the agent.

Key Terms
استطاعة الأسباب (capacity of means)
أحوال (circumstances)
اعتذار (excuse)
لغة الناس (common speech)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Everyday language confirms free will by showing people claim they 'cannot' do things.
Correction: Maturidi argues the opposite: common usage shows that 'cannot' refers to circumstantial obstacles, implying that capacity is understood as dependent on external factors, not an independent power in the agent.

B) These phrases show that capacity is understood as dependent on external circumstances, not an inner power.
C) People are unaware that God gives them capacity.
D) Such phrases prove that humans have no capacity at all.

Key Takeaway
Common speech about 'cannot' reveals that people understand capacity as contingent on circumstances, not as an autonomous power.
